1107      * <td style="text-align:center">none</td>
1108      * </tr>
1109      * <tr>
1110      * <td>{@code privateLookupIn(C1,PUB)} fails</td>
1111      * <td></td>
1112      * <td></td>
1113      * <td></td>
1114      * <td></td>
1115      * <td style="text-align:center">IAE</td>
1116      * </tr>
1117      * <tr>
1118      * <td>{@code ANY.in(X)}, for inaccessible {@code X}</td>
1119      * <td></td>
1120      * <td></td>
1121      * <td></td>
1122      * <td></td>
1123      * <td style="text-align:center">none</td>
1124      * </tr>
1125      * </tbody>
1126      * </table>
1127      *
1128      * <p>
1129      * Notes:
1130      * <ul>
1131      * <li>Class {@code C} and class {@code C1} are in module {@code M1},
1132      *     but {@code D} and {@code D2} are in module {@code M2}, and {@code E}
1133      *     is in module {@code M3}. {@code X} stands for class which is inaccessible
1134      *     to the lookup. {@code ANY} stands for any of the example lookups.</li>
1135      * <li>{@code PRO} indicates {@link #PROTECTED} bit set,
1136      *     {@code PRI} indicates {@link #PRIVATE} bit set,
1137      *     {@code PAC} indicates {@link #PACKAGE} bit set,
1138      *     {@code MOD} indicates {@link #MODULE} bit set,
1139      *     {@code 1R} and {@code 2R} indicate {@link #PUBLIC} bit set,
1140      *     {@code U} indicates {@link #UNCONDITIONAL} bit set,
1141      *     {@code IAE} indicates {@code IllegalAccessException} thrown.</li>
1142      * <li>Public access comes in three kinds:
1143      * <ul>
1144      * <li>unconditional ({@code U}): the lookup assumes readability.
1145      *     The lookup has {@code null} previous lookup class.
1146      * <li>one-module-reads ({@code 1R}): the module access checking is
1147      *     performed with respect to the lookup class.  The lookup has {@code null}
1148      *     previous lookup class.
1149      * <li>two-module-reads ({@code 2R}): the module access checking is
1150      *     performed with respect to the lookup class and the previous lookup class.
1151      *     The lookup has a non-null previous lookup class which is in a
1152      *     different module from the current lookup class.
1153      * </ul>
1154      * <li>Any attempt to reach a third module loses all access.</li>
1155      * <li>If a target class {@code X} is not accessible to {@code Lookup::in}
1156      * all access modes are dropped.</li>
1157      * </ul>
1158      *
1159      * <h2><a id="secmgr"></a>Security manager interactions</h2>
1160      * Although bytecode instructions can only refer to classes in
1161      * a related class loader, this API can search for methods in any
1162      * class, as long as a reference to its {@code Class} object is
1163      * available.  Such cross-loader references are also possible with the
1164      * Core Reflection API, and are impossible to bytecode instructions
1165      * such as {@code invokestatic} or {@code getfield}.
1166      * There is a {@linkplain java.lang.SecurityManager security manager API}
1167      * to allow applications to check such cross-loader references.
1168      * These checks apply to both the {@code MethodHandles.Lookup} API
1169      * and the Core Reflection API
1170      * (as found on {@link java.lang.Class Class}).
1171      * <p>
1172      * If a security manager is present, member and class lookups are subject to
1173      * additional checks.
1174      * From one to three calls are made to the security manager.
1175      * Any of these calls can refuse access by throwing a
1176      * {@link java.lang.SecurityException SecurityException}.
1177      * Define {@code smgr} as the security manager,
1178      * {@code lookc} as the lookup class of the current lookup object,
1179      * {@code refc} as the containing class in which the member
1180      * is being sought, and {@code defc} as the class in which the
1181      * member is actually defined.
1182      * (If a class or other type is being accessed,
1183      * the {@code refc} and {@code defc} values are the class itself.)
1184      * The value {@code lookc} is defined as <em>not present</em>
1185      * if the current lookup object does not have
1186      * {@linkplain #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege access}.
1187      * The calls are made according to the following rules:
1188      * <ul>
1189      * <li><b>Step 1:</b>
1190      *     If {@code lookc} is not present, or if its class loader is not
1191      *     the same as or an ancestor of the class loader of {@code refc},
1192      *     then {@link SecurityManager#checkPackageAccess
1193      *     smgr.checkPackageAccess(refcPkg)} is called,
1194      *     where {@code refcPkg} is the package of {@code refc}.
1195      * <li><b>Step 2a:</b>
1196      *     If the retrieved member is not public and
1197      *     {@code lookc} is not present, then
1198      *     {@link SecurityManager#checkPermission smgr.checkPermission}
1199      *     with {@code RuntimePermission("accessDeclaredMembers")} is called.
1200      * <li><b>Step 2b:</b>
1201      *     If the retrieved class has a {@code null} class loader,
1202      *     and {@code lookc} is not present, then
1203      *     {@link SecurityManager#checkPermission smgr.checkPermission}
1204      *     with {@code RuntimePermission("getClassLoader")} is called.
1205      * <li><b>Step 3:</b>
1206      *     If the retrieved member is not public,
1207      *     and if {@code lookc} is not present,
1208      *     and if {@code defc} and {@code refc} are different,
1209      *     then {@link SecurityManager#checkPackageAccess
1210      *     smgr.checkPackageAccess(defcPkg)} is called,
1211      *     where {@code defcPkg} is the package of {@code defc}.
1212      * </ul>
1213      * Security checks are performed after other access checks have passed.
1214      * Therefore, the above rules presuppose a member or class that is public,
1215      * or else that is being accessed from a lookup class that has
1216      * rights to access the member or class.
1217      * <p>
1218      * If a security manager is present and the current lookup object does not have
1219      * {@linkplain #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege access}, then
1220      * {@link #defineClass(byte[]) defineClass}
1221      * calls {@link SecurityManager#checkPermission smgr.checkPermission}
1222      * with {@code RuntimePermission("defineClass")}.
1223      *
1224      * <h2><a id="callsens"></a>Caller sensitive methods</h2>
1225      * A small number of Java methods have a special property called caller sensitivity.
1226      * A <em>caller-sensitive</em> method can behave differently depending on the
1227      * identity of its immediate caller.
1228      * <p>
1229      * If a method handle for a caller-sensitive method is requested,
1230      * the general rules for <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">bytecode behaviors</a> apply,
1231      * but they take account of the lookup class in a special way.
1232      * The resulting method handle behaves as if it were called
1233      * from an instruction contained in the lookup class,
1234      * so that the caller-sensitive method detects the lookup class.
1235      * (By contrast, the invoker of the method handle is disregarded.)
1236      * Thus, in the case of caller-sensitive methods,
1237      * different lookup classes may give rise to
1238      * differently behaving method handles.
1239      * <p>
1240      * In cases where the lookup object is
1241      * {@link MethodHandles#publicLookup() publicLookup()},
1242      * or some other lookup object without the
1243      * {@linkplain #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege access},
1244      * the lookup class is disregarded.
1245      * In such cases, no caller-sensitive method handle can be created,
1246      * access is forbidden, and the lookup fails with an
1247      * {@code IllegalAccessException}.
1248      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
1249      * <em>Discussion:</em>
1250      * For example, the caller-sensitive method
1251      * {@link java.lang.Class#forName(String) Class.forName(x)}
1252      * can return varying classes or throw varying exceptions,
1253      * depending on the class loader of the class that calls it.
1254      * A public lookup of {@code Class.forName} will fail, because
1255      * there is no reasonable way to determine its bytecode behavior.
1256      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
1257      * If an application caches method handles for broad sharing,
1258      * it should use {@code publicLookup()} to create them.
1259      * If there is a lookup of {@code Class.forName}, it will fail,
1260      * and the application must take appropriate action in that case.
1261      * It may be that a later lookup, perhaps during the invocation of a
1262      * bootstrap method, can incorporate the specific identity
1263      * of the caller, making the method accessible.
1264      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
1265      * The function {@code MethodHandles.lookup} is caller sensitive
1266      * so that there can be a secure foundation for lookups.
1267      * Nearly all other methods in the JSR 292 API rely on lookup
1268      * objects to check access requests.
1269      *
1270      * @revised 9
1271      */
1272     public static final
1273     class Lookup {
1274         /** The class on behalf of whom the lookup is being performed. */
1275         private final Class<?> lookupClass;
1276 
1277         /** previous lookup class */
1278         private final Class<?> prevLookupClass;
1279 
1280         /** The allowed sorts of members which may be looked up (PUBLIC, etc.). */
1281         private final int allowedModes;
1282 
1283         static {
1284             Reflection.registerFieldsToFilter(Lookup.class, Set.of("lookupClass", "allowedModes"));
1285         }
1286 
1287         /** A single-bit mask representing {@code public} access,
1288          *  which may contribute to the result of {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}.
1289          *  The value, {@code 0x01}, happens to be the same as the value of the
1290          *  {@code public} {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Modifier#PUBLIC modifier bit}.
1291          *  <p>
1292          *  A {@code Lookup} with this lookup mode performs cross-module access check
1293          *  with respect to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class} and
1294          *  {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class} if present.
1295          */
1296         public static final int PUBLIC = Modifier.PUBLIC;
1297 
1298         /** A single-bit mask representing {@code private} access,
1299          *  which may contribute to the result of {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}.
1300          *  The value, {@code 0x02}, happens to be the same as the value of the
1301          *  {@code private} {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Modifier#PRIVATE modifier bit}.
1302          */
1303         public static final int PRIVATE = Modifier.PRIVATE;
1304 
1305         /** A single-bit mask representing {@code protected} access,
1306          *  which may contribute to the result of {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}.
1307          *  The value, {@code 0x04}, happens to be the same as the value of the
1308          *  {@code protected} {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Modifier#PROTECTED modifier bit}.
1309          */
1310         public static final int PROTECTED = Modifier.PROTECTED;
1311 
1312         /** A single-bit mask representing {@code package} access (default access),
1313          *  which may contribute to the result of {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}.
1314          *  The value is {@code 0x08}, which does not correspond meaningfully to
1315          *  any particular {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Modifier modifier bit}.
1316          */
1317         public static final int PACKAGE = Modifier.STATIC;
1318 
1319         /** A single-bit mask representing {@code module} access,
1320          *  which may contribute to the result of {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}.
1321          *  The value is {@code 0x10}, which does not correspond meaningfully to
1322          *  any particular {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Modifier modifier bit}.
1323          *  In conjunction with the {@code PUBLIC} modifier bit, a {@code Lookup}
1324          *  with this lookup mode can access all public types in the module of the
1325          *  lookup class and public types in packages exported by other modules
1326          *  to the module of the lookup class.
1327          *  <p>
1328          *  If this lookup mode is set, the {@linkplain #previousLookupClass()
1329          *  previous lookup class} is always {@code null}.
1330          *
1331          *  @since 9
1332          *  @spec JPMS
1333          */
1334         public static final int MODULE = PACKAGE << 1;
1335 
1336         /** A single-bit mask representing {@code unconditional} access
1337          *  which may contribute to the result of {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}.
1338          *  The value is {@code 0x20}, which does not correspond meaningfully to
1339          *  any particular {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Modifier modifier bit}.
1340          *  A {@code Lookup} with this lookup mode assumes {@linkplain
1341          *  java.lang.Module#canRead(java.lang.Module) readability}.
1342          *  This lookup mode can access all public members of public types
1343          *  of all modules when the type is in a package that is {@link
1344          *  java.lang.Module#isExported(String) exported unconditionally}.
1345          *
1346          *  <p>
1347          *  If this lookup mode is set, the {@linkplain #previousLookupClass()
1348          *  previous lookup class} is always {@code null}.
1349          *
1350          *  @since 9
1351          *  @spec JPMS
1352          *  @see #publicLookup()
1353          */
1354         public static final int UNCONDITIONAL = PACKAGE << 2;
1355 
1356         private static final int ALL_MODES = (PUBLIC | PRIVATE | PROTECTED | PACKAGE | MODULE | UNCONDITIONAL);
1357         private static final int FULL_POWER_MODES = (ALL_MODES & ~UNCONDITIONAL);
1358         private static final int TRUSTED   = -1;
1359 
1360         /*
1361          * Adjust PUBLIC => PUBLIC|MODULE|UNCONDITIONAL
1362          * Adjust 0 => PACKAGE
1363          */
1364         private static int fixmods(int mods) {
1365             mods &= (ALL_MODES - PACKAGE - MODULE - UNCONDITIONAL);
1366             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
1367                 mods |= UNCONDITIONAL;
1368             return (mods != 0) ? mods : PACKAGE;
1369         }
1370 
1371         /** Tells which class is performing the lookup.  It is this class against
1372          *  which checks are performed for visibility and access permissions.
1373          *  <p>
1374          *  If this lookup object has a {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
1375          *  access checks are performed against both the lookup class and the previous lookup class.
1376          *  <p>
1377          *  The class implies a maximum level of access permission,
1378          *  but the permissions may be additionally limited by the bitmask
1379          *  {@link #lookupModes lookupModes}, which controls whether non-public members
1380          *  can be accessed.
1381          *  @return the lookup class, on behalf of which this lookup object finds members
1382          *  @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
1383          */
1384         public Class<?> lookupClass() {
1385             return lookupClass;
1386         }
1387 
1388         /** Reports a lookup class in another module that this lookup object
1389          * was previously teleported from, or {@code null}.
1390          * <p>
1391          * A {@code Lookup} object produced by the factory methods, such as the
1392          * {@link #lookup() lookup()} and {@link #publicLookup() publicLookup()} method,
1393          * has {@code null} previous lookup class.
1394          * A {@code Lookup} object has a non-null previous lookup class
1395          * when this lookup was teleported from an old lookup class
1396          * in one module to a new lookup class in another module.
1397          *
1398          * @return the lookup class in another module that this lookup object was
1399          *         previously teleported from, or {@code null}
1400          * @since 14
1401          * @see #in(Class)
1402          * @see MethodHandles#privateLookupIn(Class, Lookup)
1403          * @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
1404          */
1405         public Class<?> previousLookupClass() {
1406             return prevLookupClass;
1407         }
1408 
1409         // This is just for calling out to MethodHandleImpl.
1410         private Class<?> lookupClassOrNull() {
1411             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED) {
1412                 return null;
1413             }
1414             if (allowedModes == UNCONDITIONAL) {
1415                 // use Object as the caller to pass to VM doing resolution
1416                 return Object.class;
1417             }
1418             return lookupClass;
1419         }
1420 
1421         /** Tells which access-protection classes of members this lookup object can produce.
1422          *  The result is a bit-mask of the bits
1423          *  {@linkplain #PUBLIC PUBLIC (0x01)},
1424          *  {@linkplain #PRIVATE PRIVATE (0x02)},
1425          *  {@linkplain #PROTECTED PROTECTED (0x04)},
1426          *  {@linkplain #PACKAGE PACKAGE (0x08)},
1427          *  {@linkplain #MODULE MODULE (0x10)},
1428          *  and {@linkplain #UNCONDITIONAL UNCONDITIONAL (0x20)}.
1429          *  <p>
1430          *  A freshly-created lookup object
1431          *  on the {@linkplain java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#lookup() caller's class} has
1432          *  all possible bits set, except {@code UNCONDITIONAL}.
1433          *  A lookup object on a new lookup class
1434          *  {@linkplain java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.Lookup#in created from a previous lookup object}
1435          *  may have some mode bits set to zero.
1436          *  Mode bits can also be
1437          *  {@linkplain java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.Lookup#dropLookupMode directly cleared}.
1438          *  Once cleared, mode bits cannot be restored from the downgraded lookup object.
1439          *  The purpose of this is to restrict access via the new lookup object,
1440          *  so that it can access only names which can be reached by the original
1441          *  lookup object, and also by the new lookup class.
1442          *  @return the lookup modes, which limit the kinds of access performed by this lookup object
1443          *  @see #in
1444          *  @see #dropLookupMode
1445          *
1446          *  @revised 9
1447          *  @spec JPMS
1448          */
1449         public int lookupModes() {
1450             return allowedModes & ALL_MODES;
1451         }
1452 
1453         /** Embody the current class (the lookupClass) as a lookup class
1454          * for method handle creation.
1455          * Must be called by from a method in this package,
1456          * which in turn is called by a method not in this package.
1457          */
1458         Lookup(Class<?> lookupClass) {
1459             this(lookupClass, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
1460         }
1461 
1462         private Lookup(Class<?> lookupClass, Class<?> prevLookupClass, int allowedModes) {
1463             assert prevLookupClass == null || ((allowedModes & MODULE) == 0
1464                     && prevLookupClass.getModule() != lookupClass.getModule());
1465             assert !lookupClass.isArray() && !lookupClass.isPrimitive();
1466             this.lookupClass = lookupClass;
1467             this.prevLookupClass = prevLookupClass;
1468             this.allowedModes = allowedModes;
1469         }
1470 
1471         private static Lookup newLookup(Class<?> lookupClass, Class<?> prevLookupClass, int allowedModes) {
1472             // make sure we haven't accidentally picked up a privileged class:
1473             checkUnprivilegedlookupClass(lookupClass);
1474             return new Lookup(lookupClass, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
1475         }
1476 
1477         /**
1478          * Creates a lookup on the specified new lookup class.
1479          * The resulting object will report the specified
1480          * class as its own {@link #lookupClass() lookupClass}.
1481          *
1482          * <p>
1483          * However, the resulting {@code Lookup} object is guaranteed
1484          * to have no more access capabilities than the original.
1485          * In particular, access capabilities can be lost as follows:<ul>
1486          * <li>If the new lookup class is in a different module from the old one,
1487          * i.e. {@link #MODULE MODULE} access is lost.
1488          * <li>If the new lookup class is in a different package
1489          * than the old one, protected and default (package) members will not be accessible,
1490          * i.e. {@link #PROTECTED PROTECTED} and {@link #PACKAGE PACKAGE} access are lost.
1491          * <li>If the new lookup class is not within the same package member
1492          * as the old one, private members will not be accessible, and protected members
1493          * will not be accessible by virtue of inheritance,
1494          * i.e. {@link #PRIVATE PRIVATE} access is lost.
1495          * (Protected members may continue to be accessible because of package sharing.)
1496          * <li>If the new lookup class is not
1497          * {@linkplain #accessClass(Class) accessible} to this lookup,
1498          * then no members, not even public members, will be accessible
1499          * i.e. all access modes are lost.
1500          * <li>If the new lookup class, the old lookup class and the previous lookup class
1501          * are all in different modules i.e. teleporting to a third module,
1502          * all access modes are lost.
1503          * </ul>
1504          * <p>
1505          * The new previous lookup class is chosen as follows:
1506          * <ul>
1507          * <li>If the new lookup object has {@link #UNCONDITIONAL UNCONDITIONAL} bit,
1508          * the new previous lookup class is {@code null}.
1509          * <li>If the new lookup class is in the same module as the old lookup class,
1510          * the new previous lookup class is the old previous lookup class.
1511          * <li>If the new lookup class is in a different module from the old lookup class,
1512          * the new previous lookup class is the old lookup class.
1513          *</ul>
1514          * <p>
1515          * The resulting lookup's capabilities for loading classes
1516          * (used during {@link #findClass} invocations)
1517          * are determined by the lookup class' loader,
1518          * which may change due to this operation.
1519          * <p>
1520          * @param requestedLookupClass the desired lookup class for the new lookup object
1521          * @return a lookup object which reports the desired lookup class, or the same object
1522          * if there is no change
1523          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code requestedLookupClass} is a primitive type or void or array class
1524          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
1525          *
1526          * @revised 9
1527          * @spec JPMS
1528          * @see #accessClass(Class)
1529          * @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
1530          */
1531         public Lookup in(Class<?> requestedLookupClass) {
1532             Objects.requireNonNull(requestedLookupClass);
1533             if (requestedLookupClass.isPrimitive())
1534                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(requestedLookupClass + " is a primitive class");
1535             if (requestedLookupClass.isArray())
1536                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(requestedLookupClass + " is an array class");
1537 
1538             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  // IMPL_LOOKUP can make any lookup at all
1539                 return new Lookup(requestedLookupClass, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
1540             if (requestedLookupClass == this.lookupClass)
1541                 return this;  // keep same capabilities
1542             int newModes = (allowedModes & FULL_POWER_MODES);
1543             Module fromModule = this.lookupClass.getModule();
1544             Module targetModule = requestedLookupClass.getModule();
1545             Class<?> plc = this.previousLookupClass();
1546             if ((this.allowedModes & UNCONDITIONAL) != 0) {
1547                 assert plc == null;
1548                 newModes = UNCONDITIONAL;
1549             } else if (fromModule != targetModule) {
1550                 if (plc != null && !VerifyAccess.isSameModule(plc, requestedLookupClass)) {
1551                     // allow hopping back and forth between fromModule and plc's module
1552                     // but not the third module
1553                     newModes = 0;
1554                 }
1555                 // drop MODULE access
1556                 newModes &= ~(MODULE|PACKAGE|PRIVATE|PROTECTED);
1557                 // teleport from this lookup class
1558                 plc = this.lookupClass;
1559             }
1560             if ((newModes & PACKAGE) != 0
1561                 && !VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(this.lookupClass, requestedLookupClass)) {
1562                 newModes &= ~(PACKAGE|PRIVATE|PROTECTED);
1563             }
1564             // Allow nestmate lookups to be created without special privilege:
1565             if ((newModes & PRIVATE) != 0
1566                     && !VerifyAccess.isSamePackageMember(this.lookupClass, requestedLookupClass)) {
1567                 newModes &= ~(PRIVATE|PROTECTED);
1568             }
1569             if ((newModes & (PUBLIC|UNCONDITIONAL)) != 0
1570                 && !VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(requestedLookupClass, this.lookupClass, this.prevLookupClass, allowedModes)) {
1571                 // The requested class it not accessible from the lookup class.
1572                 // No permissions.
1573                 newModes = 0;
1574             }
1575             return newLookup(requestedLookupClass, plc, newModes);
1576         }
1577 
1578         /**
1579          * Creates a lookup on the same lookup class which this lookup object
1580          * finds members, but with a lookup mode that has lost the given lookup mode.
1581          * The lookup mode to drop is one of {@link #PUBLIC PUBLIC}, {@link #MODULE
1582          * MODULE}, {@link #PACKAGE PACKAGE}, {@link #PROTECTED PROTECTED},
1583          * {@link #PRIVATE PRIVATE}, or {@link #UNCONDITIONAL UNCONDITIONAL}.
1584          *
1585          * <p> If this lookup is a {@linkplain MethodHandles#publicLookup() public lookup},
1586          * this lookup has {@code UNCONDITIONAL} mode set and it has no other mode set.
1587          * When dropping {@code UNCONDITIONAL} on a public lookup then the resulting
1588          * lookup has no access.
1589          *
1590          * <p> If this lookup is not a public lookup, then the following applies
1591          * regardless of its {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes}.
1592          * {@link #PROTECTED PROTECTED} is always dropped and so the resulting lookup
1593          * mode will never have this access capability. When dropping {@code PACKAGE}
1594          * then the resulting lookup will not have {@code PACKAGE} or {@code PRIVATE}
1595          * access. When dropping {@code MODULE} then the resulting lookup will not
1596          * have {@code MODULE}, {@code PACKAGE}, or {@code PRIVATE} access.
1597          * When dropping {@code PUBLIC} then the resulting lookup has no access.
1598          *
1599          * @apiNote
1600          * A lookup with {@code PACKAGE} but not {@code PRIVATE} mode can safely
1601          * delegate non-public access within the package of the lookup class without
1602          * conferring  <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>.
1603          * A lookup with {@code MODULE} but not
1604          * {@code PACKAGE} mode can safely delegate {@code PUBLIC} access within
1605          * the module of the lookup class without conferring package access.
1606          * A lookup with a {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class}
1607          * (and {@code PUBLIC} but not {@code MODULE} mode) can safely delegate access
1608          * to public classes accessible to both the module of the lookup class
1609          * and the module of the previous lookup class.
1610          *
1611          * @param modeToDrop the lookup mode to drop
1612          * @return a lookup object which lacks the indicated mode, or the same object if there is no change
1613          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code modeToDrop} is not one of {@code PUBLIC},
1614          * {@code MODULE}, {@code PACKAGE}, {@code PROTECTED}, {@code PRIVATE} or {@code UNCONDITIONAL}
1615          * @see MethodHandles#privateLookupIn
1616          * @since 9
1617          */
1618         public Lookup dropLookupMode(int modeToDrop) {
1619             int oldModes = lookupModes();
1620             int newModes = oldModes & ~(modeToDrop | PROTECTED);
1621             switch (modeToDrop) {
1622                 case PUBLIC: newModes &= ~(FULL_POWER_MODES); break;
1623                 case MODULE: newModes &= ~(PACKAGE | PRIVATE); break;
1624                 case PACKAGE: newModes &= ~(PRIVATE); break;
1625                 case PROTECTED:
1626                 case PRIVATE:
1627                 case UNCONDITIONAL: break;
1628                 default: throw new IllegalArgumentException(modeToDrop + " is not a valid mode to drop");
1629             }
1630             if (newModes == oldModes) return this;  // return self if no change
1631             return newLookup(lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), newModes);
1632         }
1633 
1634         /**
1635          * Creates and links a class or interface from {@code bytes}
1636          * with the same class loader and in the same runtime package and
1637          * {@linkplain java.security.ProtectionDomain protection domain} as this lookup's
1638          * {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class} as if calling
1639          * {@link ClassLoader#defineClass(String,byte[],int,int,ProtectionDomain)
1640          * ClassLoader::defineClass}.
1641          *
1642          * <p> The {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes} for this lookup must include
1643          * {@link #PACKAGE PACKAGE} access as default (package) members will be
1644          * accessible to the class. The {@code PACKAGE} lookup mode serves to authenticate
1645          * that the lookup object was created by a caller in the runtime package (or derived
1646          * from a lookup originally created by suitably privileged code to a target class in
1647          * the runtime package). </p>
1648          *
1649          * <p> The {@code bytes} parameter is the class bytes of a valid class file (as defined
1650          * by the <em>The Java Virtual Machine Specification</em>) with a class name in the
1651          * same package as the lookup class. </p>
1652          *
1653          * <p> This method does not run the class initializer. The class initializer may
1654          * run at a later time, as detailed in section 12.4 of the <em>The Java Language
1655          * Specification</em>. </p>
1656          *
1657          * <p> If there is a security manager and this lookup does not have {@linkplain
1658          * #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege access}, its {@code checkPermission} method
1659          * is first called to check {@code RuntimePermission("defineClass")}. </p>
1660          *
1661          * @param bytes the class bytes
1662          * @return the {@code Class} object for the class
1663          * @throws IllegalAccessException if this lookup does not have {@code PACKAGE} access
1664          * @throws ClassFormatError if {@code bytes} is not a {@code ClassFile} structure
1665          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code bytes} denotes a class in a different package
1666          * than the lookup class or {@code bytes} is not a class or interface
1667          * ({@code ACC_MODULE} flag is set in the value of the {@code access_flags} item)
1668          * @throws VerifyError if the newly created class cannot be verified
1669          * @throws LinkageError if the newly created class cannot be linked for any other reason
1670          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
1671          *                           <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
1672          * @throws NullPointerException if {@code bytes} is {@code null}
1673          * @since 9
1674          * @spec JPMS
1675          * @see Lookup#privateLookupIn
1676          * @see Lookup#dropLookupMode
1677          * @see ClassLoader#defineClass(String,byte[],int,int,ProtectionDomain)
1678          */
1679         public Class<?> defineClass(byte[] bytes) throws IllegalAccessException {
1680             ensureDefineClassPermission();
1681             if ((lookupModes() & PACKAGE) == 0)
1682                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Lookup does not have PACKAGE access");
1683             return makeClassDefiner(bytes.clone()).defineClass(false);
1684         }
1685 
1686         private void ensureDefineClassPermission() {
1687             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
1688 
1689             if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
1690                 SecurityManager sm = System.getSecurityManager();
1691                 if (sm != null)
1692                     sm.checkPermission(new RuntimePermission("defineClass"));
1693             }
1694         }
1695 
1696         /**
1697          * The set of class options that specify whether a hidden class created by
1698          * {@link Lookup#defineHiddenClass(byte[], boolean, ClassOption...)
1699          * Lookup::defineHiddenClass} method is dynamically added as a new member
1700          * to the nest of a lookup class and/or whether a hidden class has
1701          * a strong relationship with the class loader marked as its defining loader.
1702          *
1703          * @since 15
1704          */
1705         public enum ClassOption {
1706             /**
1707              * Specifies that a hidden class be added to {@linkplain Class#getNestHost nest}
1708              * of a lookup class as a nestmate.
1709              *
1710              * <p> A hidden nestmate class has access to the private members of all
1711              * classes and interfaces in the same nest.
1712              *
1713              * @see Class#getNestHost()
1714              */
1715             NESTMATE(NESTMATE_CLASS),
1716 
1717             /**
1718              * Specifies that a hidden class has a <em>strong</em>
1719              * relationship with the class loader marked as its defining loader,
1720              * as a normal class or interface has with its own defining loader.
1721              * This means that the hidden class may be unloaded if and only if
1722              * its defining loader is not reachable and thus may be reclaimed
1723              * by a garbage collector (JLS 12.7).
1724              *
1725              * <p> By default, a hidden class or interface may be unloaded
1726              * even if the class loader that is marked as its defining loader is
1727              * <a href="../ref/package.html#reachability">reachable</a>.
1728 
1729              *
1730              * @jls 12.7 Unloading of Classes and Interfaces
1731              */
1732             STRONG(STRONG_LOADER_LINK);
1733 
1734             /* the flag value is used by VM at define class time */
1735             private final int flag;
1736             ClassOption(int flag) {
1737                 this.flag = flag;
1738             }
1739 
1740             static int optionsToFlag(Set<ClassOption> options) {
1741                 int flags = 0;
1742                 for (ClassOption cp : options) {
1743                     flags |= cp.flag;
1744                 }
1745                 return flags;
1746             }
1747         }
1748 
1749         /**
1750          * Creates a <em>hidden</em> class or interface from {@code bytes},
1751          * returning a {@code Lookup} on the newly created class or interface.
1752          *
1753          * <p> Ordinarily, a class or interface {@code C} is created by a class loader,
1754          * which either defines {@code C} directly or delegates to another class loader.
1755          * A class loader defines {@code C} directly by invoking
1756          * {@link ClassLoader#defineClass(String, byte[], int, int, ProtectionDomain)
1757          * ClassLoader::defineClass}, which causes the Java Virtual Machine
1758          * to derive {@code C} from a purported representation in {@code class} file format.
1759          * In situations where use of a class loader is undesirable, a class or interface
1760          * {@code C} can be created by this method instead. This method is capable of
1761          * defining {@code C}, and thereby creating it, without invoking
1762          * {@code ClassLoader::defineClass}.
1763          * Instead, this method defines {@code C} as if by arranging for
1764          * the Java Virtual Machine to derive a nonarray class or interface {@code C}
1765          * from a purported representation in {@code class} file format
1766          * using the following rules:
1767          *
1768          * <ol>
1769          * <li> The {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes} for this {@code Lookup}
1770          * must include {@linkplain #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege} access.
1771          * This level of access is needed to create {@code C} in the module
1772          * of the lookup class of this {@code Lookup}.</li>
1773          *
1774          * <li> The purported representation in {@code bytes} must be a {@code ClassFile}
1775          * structure of a supported major and minor version. The major and minor version
1776          * may differ from the {@code class} file version of the lookup class of this
1777          * {@code Lookup}.</li>
1778          *
1779          * <li> The value of {@code this_class} must be a valid index in the
1780          * {@code constant_pool} table, and the entry at that index must be a valid
1781          * {@code CONSTANT_Class_info} structure. Let {@code N} be the binary name
1782          * encoded in internal form that is specified by this structure. {@code N} must
1783          * denote a class or interface in the same package as the lookup class.</li>
1784          *
1785          * <li> Let {@code CN} be the string {@code N + "." + <suffix>},
1786          * where {@code <suffix>} is an unqualified name.
1787          *
1788          * <p> Let {@code newBytes} be the {@code ClassFile} structure given by
1789          * {@code bytes} with an additional entry in the {@code constant_pool} table,
1790          * indicating a {@code CONSTANT_Utf8_info} structure for {@code CN}, and
1791          * where the {@code CONSTANT_Class_info} structure indicated by {@code this_class}
1792          * refers to the new {@code CONSTANT_Utf8_info} structure.
1793          *
1794          * <p> Let {@code L} be the defining class loader of the lookup class of this {@code Lookup}.
1795          *
1796          * <p> {@code C} is derived with name {@code CN}, class loader {@code L}, and
1797          * purported representation {@code newBytes} as if by the rules of JVMS {@jvms 5.3.5},
1798          * with the following adjustments:
1799          * <ul>
1800          * <li> The constant indicated by {@code this_class} is permitted to specify a name
1801          * that includes a single {@code "."} character, even though this is not a valid
1802          * binary class or interface name in internal form.</li>
1803          *
1804          * <li> The Java Virtual Machine marks {@code L} as the defining class loader of {@code C},
1805          * but no class loader is recorded as an initiating class loader of {@code C}.</li>
1806          *
1807          * <li> {@code C} is considered to have the same runtime
1808          * {@linkplain Class#getPackage() package}, {@linkplain Class#getModule() module}
1809          * and {@linkplain java.security.ProtectionDomain protection domain}
1810          * as the lookup class of this {@code Lookup}.
1811          * <li> Let {@code GN} be the binary name obtained by taking {@code N}
1812          * (a binary name encoded in internal form) and replacing ASCII forward slashes with
1813          * ASCII periods. For the instance of {@link java.lang.Class} representing {@code C}:
1814          * <ul>
1815          * <li> {@link Class#getName()} returns the string {@code GN + "/" + <suffix>},
1816          *      even though this is not a valid binary class or interface name.</li>
1817          * <li> {@link Class#descriptorString()} returns the string
1818          *      {@code "L" + N + "." + <suffix> + ";"},
1819          *      even though this is not a valid type descriptor name.</li>
1820          * <li> {@link Class#describeConstable()} returns an empty optional as {@code C}
1821          *      cannot be described in {@linkplain java.lang.constant.ClassDesc nominal form}.</li>
1822          * </ul>
1823          * </ul>
1824          * </li>
1825          * </ol>
1826          *
1827          * <p> After {@code C} is derived, it is linked by the Java Virtual Machine.
1828          * Linkage occurs as specified in JVMS {@jvms 5.4.3}, with the following adjustments:
1829          * <ul>
1830          * <li> During verification, whenever it is necessary to load the class named
1831          * {@code CN}, the attempt succeeds, producing class {@code C}. No request is
1832          * made of any class loader.</li>
1833          *
1834          * <li> On any attempt to resolve the entry in the run-time constant pool indicated
1835          * by {@code this_class}, the symbolic reference is considered to be resolved to
1836          * {@code C} and resolution always succeeds immediately.</li>
1837          * </ul>
1838          *
1839          * <p> If the {@code initialize} parameter is {@code true},
1840          * then {@code C} is initialized by the Java Virtual Machine.
1841          *
1842          * <p> The newly created class or interface {@code C} serves as the
1843          * {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class} of the {@code Lookup} object
1844          * returned by this method. {@code C} is <em>hidden</em> in the sense that
1845          * no other class or interface can refer to {@code C} via a constant pool entry.
1846          * That is, a hidden class or interface cannot be named as a supertype, a field type,
1847          * a method parameter type, or a method return type by any other class.
1848          * This is because a hidden class or interface does not have a binary name, so
1849          * there is no internal form available to record in any class's constant pool.
1850          * A hidden class or interface is not discoverable by {@link Class#forName(String, boolean, ClassLoader)},
1851          * {@link ClassLoader#loadClass(String, boolean)}, or {@link #findClass(String)}, and
1852          * is not {@linkplain java.lang.instrument.Instrumentation#isModifiableClass(Class)
1853          * modifiable} by Java agents or tool agents using the <a href="{@docRoot}/../specs/jvmti.html">
1854          * JVM Tool Interface</a>.
1855          *
1856          * <p> A class or interface created by
1857          * {@linkplain ClassLoader#defineClass(String, byte[], int, int, ProtectionDomain)
1858          * a class loader} has a strong relationship with that class loader.
1859          * That is, every {@code Class} object contains a reference to the {@code ClassLoader}
1860          * that {@linkplain Class#getClassLoader() defined it}.
1861          * This means that a class created by a class loader may be unloaded if and
1862          * only if its defining loader is not reachable and thus may be reclaimed
1863          * by a garbage collector (JLS 12.7).
1864          *
1865          * By default, however, a hidden class or interface may be unloaded even if
1866          * the class loader that is marked as its defining loader is
1867          * <a href="../ref/package.html#reachability">reachable</a>.
1868          * This behavior is useful when a hidden class or interface serves multiple
1869          * classes defined by arbitrary class loaders.  In other cases, a hidden
1870          * class or interface may be linked to a single class (or a small number of classes)
1871          * with the same defining loader as the hidden class or interface.
1872          * In such cases, where the hidden class or interface must be coterminous
1873          * with a normal class or interface, the {@link ClassOption#STRONG STRONG}
1874          * option may be passed in {@code options}.
1875          * This arranges for a hidden class to have the same strong relationship
1876          * with the class loader marked as its defining loader,
1877          * as a normal class or interface has with its own defining loader.
1878          *
1879          * If {@code STRONG} is not used, then the invoker of {@code defineHiddenClass}
1880          * may still prevent a hidden class or interface from being
1881          * unloaded by ensuring that the {@code Class} object is reachable.
1882          *
1883          * <p> The unloading characteristics are set for each hidden class when it is
1884          * defined, and cannot be changed later.  An advantage of allowing hidden classes
1885          * to be unloaded independently of the class loader marked as their defining loader
1886          * is that a very large number of hidden classes may be created by an application.
1887          * In contrast, if {@code STRONG} is used, then the JVM may run out of memory,
1888          * just as if normal classes were created by class loaders.
1889          *
1890          * <p> Classes and interfaces in a nest are allowed to have mutual access to
1891          * their private members.  The nest relationship is determined by
1892          * the {@code NestHost} attribute (JVMS {@jvms 4.7.28}) and
1893          * the {@code NestMembers} attribute (JVMS {@jvms 4.7.29}) in a {@code class} file.
1894          * By default, a hidden class belongs to a nest consisting only of itself
1895          * because a hidden class has no binary name.
1896          * The {@link ClassOption#NESTMATE NESTMATE} option can be passed in {@code options}
1897          * to create a hidden class or interface {@code C} as a member of a nest.
1898          * The nest to which {@code C} belongs is not based on any {@code NestHost} attribute
1899          * in the {@code ClassFile} structure from which {@code C} was derived.
1900          * Instead, the following rules determine the nest host of {@code C}:
1901          * <ul>
1902          * <li>If the nest host of the lookup class of this {@code Lookup} has previously
1903          *     been determined, then let {@code H} be the nest host of the lookup class.
1904          *     Otherwise, the nest host of the lookup class is determined using the
1905          *     algorithm in JVMS {@jvms 5.4.4}, yielding {@code H}.</li>
1906          * <li>The nest host of {@code C} is determined to be {@code H},
1907          *     the nest host of the lookup class.</li>
1908          * </ul>
1909          *
1910          * <p> A hidden class or interface may be serializable, but this requires a custom
1911          * serialization mechanism in order to ensure that instances are properly serialized
1912          * and deserialized. The default serialization mechanism supports only classes and
1913          * interfaces that are discoverable by their class name.
1914          *
1915          * @param bytes the bytes that make up the class data,
1916          * in the format of a valid {@code class} file as defined by
1917          * <cite>The Java Virtual Machine Specification</cite>.
1918          * @param initialize if {@code true} the class will be initialized.
1919          * @param options {@linkplain ClassOption class options}
1920          * @return the {@code Lookup} object on the hidden class
1921          *
1922          * @throws IllegalAccessException if this {@code Lookup} does not have
1923          * {@linkplain #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege} access
1924          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
1925          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
1926          * @throws ClassFormatError if {@code bytes} is not a {@code ClassFile} structure
1927          * @throws UnsupportedClassVersionError if {@code bytes} is not of a supported major or minor version
1928          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code bytes} denotes a class in a different package
1929          * than the lookup class or {@code bytes} is not a class or interface
1930          * ({@code ACC_MODULE} flag is set in the value of the {@code access_flags} item)
1931          * @throws IncompatibleClassChangeError if the class or interface named as
1932          * the direct superclass of {@code C} is in fact an interface, or if any of the classes
1933          * or interfaces named as direct superinterfaces of {@code C} are not in fact interfaces
1934          * @throws ClassCircularityError if any of the superclasses or superinterfaces of
1935          * {@code C} is {@code C} itself
1936          * @throws VerifyError if the newly created class cannot be verified
1937          * @throws LinkageError if the newly created class cannot be linked for any other reason
1938          * @throws NullPointerException if any parameter is {@code null}
1939          *
1940          * @since 15
1941          * @see Class#isHidden()
1942          * @jvms 4.2.1 Binary Class and Interface Names
1943          * @jvms 4.2.2 Unqualified Names
1944          * @jvms 4.7.28 The {@code NestHost} Attribute
1945          * @jvms 4.7.29 The {@code NestMembers} Attribute
1946          * @jvms 5.4.3.1 Class and Interface Resolution
1947          * @jvms 5.4.4 Access Control
1948          * @jvms 5.3.5 Deriving a {@code Class} from a {@code class} File Representation
1949          * @jvms 5.4 Linking
1950          * @jvms 5.5 Initialization
1951          * @jls 12.7 Unloading of Classes and Interfaces
1952          */
1953         public Lookup defineHiddenClass(byte[] bytes, boolean initialize, ClassOption... options)
1954                 throws IllegalAccessException
1955         {
1956             Objects.requireNonNull(bytes);
1957             Objects.requireNonNull(options);
1958 
1959             ensureDefineClassPermission();
1960             if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
1961                 throw new IllegalAccessException(this + " does not have full privilege access");
1962             }
1963 
1964             return makeHiddenClassDefiner(bytes.clone(), Set.of(options), false).defineClassAsLookup(initialize);
1965         }
1966 
1967         /**
1968          * Creates a <em>hidden</em> class or interface from {@code bytes} with associated
1969          * {@linkplain MethodHandles#classData(Lookup, String, Class) class data},
1970          * returning a {@code Lookup} on the newly created class or interface.
1971          *
1972          * <p> This method is equivalent to calling
1973          * {@link #defineHiddenClass(byte[], boolean, ClassOption...) defineHiddenClass(bytes, true, options)}
1974          * as if the hidden class has a private static final unnamed field whose value
1975          * is initialized to {@code classData} right before the class initializer is
1976          * executed.  The newly created class is linked and initialized by the Java
1977          * Virtual Machine.
1978          *
1979          * <p> The {@link MethodHandles#classData(Lookup, String, Class) MethodHandles::classData}
1980          * method can be used to retrieve the {@code classData}.
1981          *
1982          * @param bytes     the class bytes
1983          * @param classData pre-initialized class data
1984          * @param options   {@linkplain ClassOption class options}
1985          * @return the {@code Lookup} object on the hidden class
1986          *
1987          * @throws IllegalAccessException if this {@code Lookup} does not have
1988          * {@linkplain #hasFullPrivilegeAccess() full privilege} access
1989          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
1990          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
1991          * @throws ClassFormatError if {@code bytes} is not a {@code ClassFile} structure
1992          * @throws UnsupportedClassVersionError if {@code bytes} is not of a supported major or minor version
1993          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code bytes} denotes a class in a different package
1994          * than the lookup class or {@code bytes} is not a class or interface
1995          * ({@code ACC_MODULE} flag is set in the value of the {@code access_flags} item)
1996          * @throws IncompatibleClassChangeError if the class or interface named as
1997          * the direct superclass of {@code C} is in fact an interface, or if any of the classes
1998          * or interfaces named as direct superinterfaces of {@code C} are not in fact interfaces
1999          * @throws ClassCircularityError if any of the superclasses or superinterfaces of
2000          * {@code C} is {@code C} itself
2001          * @throws VerifyError if the newly created class cannot be verified
2002          * @throws LinkageError if the newly created class cannot be linked for any other reason
2003          * @throws NullPointerException if any parameter is {@code null}
2004          *
2005          * @since 15
2006          * @see Lookup#defineHiddenClass(byte[], boolean, ClassOption...)
2007          * @see Class#isHidden()
2008          */
2009         /* package-private */ Lookup defineHiddenClassWithClassData(byte[] bytes, Object classData, ClassOption... options)
2010                 throws IllegalAccessException
2011         {
2012             Objects.requireNonNull(bytes);
2013             Objects.requireNonNull(classData);
2014             Objects.requireNonNull(options);
2015 
2016             ensureDefineClassPermission();
2017             if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
2018                 throw new IllegalAccessException(this + " does not have full privilege access");
2019             }
2020 
2021             return makeHiddenClassDefiner(bytes.clone(), Set.of(options), false)
2022                        .defineClassAsLookup(true, classData);
2023         }
2024 
2025         static class ClassFile {
2026             final String name;
2027             final int accessFlags;
2028             final byte[] bytes;
2029             ClassFile(String name, int accessFlags, byte[] bytes) {
2030                 this.name = name;
2031                 this.accessFlags = accessFlags;
2032                 this.bytes = bytes;
2033             }
2034 
2035             static ClassFile newInstanceNoCheck(String name, byte[] bytes) {
2036                 return new ClassFile(name, 0, bytes);
2037             }
2038 
2039             /**
2040              * This method checks the class file version and the structure of `this_class`.
2041              * and checks if the bytes is a class or interface (ACC_MODULE flag not set)
2042              * that is in the named package.
2043              *
2044              * @throws IllegalArgumentException if ACC_MODULE flag is set in access flags
2045              * or the class is not in the given package name.
2046              */
2047             static ClassFile newInstance(byte[] bytes, String pkgName) {
2048                 int magic = readInt(bytes, 0);
2049                 if (magic != 0xCAFEBABE) {
2050                     throw new ClassFormatError("Incompatible magic value: " + magic);
2051                 }
2052                 int minor = readUnsignedShort(bytes, 4);
2053                 int major = readUnsignedShort(bytes, 6);
2054                 if (!VM.isSupportedClassFileVersion(major, minor)) {
2055                     throw new UnsupportedClassVersionError("Unsupported class file version " + major + "." + minor);
2056                 }
2057 
2058                 String name;
2059                 int accessFlags;
2060                 try {
2061                     ClassReader reader = new ClassReader(bytes);
2062                     // ClassReader::getClassName does not check if `this_class` is CONSTANT_Class_info
2063                     // workaround to read `this_class` using readConst and validate the value
2064                     int thisClass = reader.readUnsignedShort(reader.header + 2);
2065                     Object constant = reader.readConst(thisClass, new char[reader.getMaxStringLength()]);
2066                     if (!(constant instanceof Type)) {
2067                         throw new ClassFormatError("this_class item: #" + thisClass + " not a CONSTANT_Class_info");
2068                     }
2069                     Type type = ((Type) constant);
2070                     if (!type.getDescriptor().startsWith("L")) {
2071                         throw new ClassFormatError("this_class item: #" + thisClass + " not a CONSTANT_Class_info");
2072                     }
2073                     name = type.getClassName();
2074                     accessFlags = reader.readUnsignedShort(reader.header);
2075                 } catch (RuntimeException e) {
2076                     // ASM exceptions are poorly specified
2077                     ClassFormatError cfe = new ClassFormatError();
2078                     cfe.initCause(e);
2079                     throw cfe;
2080                 }
2081 
2082                 // must be a class or interface
2083                 if ((accessFlags & Opcodes.ACC_MODULE) != 0) {
2084                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("Not a class or interface: ACC_MODULE flag is set");
2085                 }
2086 
2087                 // check if it's in the named package
2088                 int index = name.lastIndexOf('.');
2089                 String pn = (index == -1) ? "" : name.substring(0, index);
2090                 if (!pn.equals(pkgName)) {
2091                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(name + " not in same package as lookup class");

2092                 }
2093 
2094                 return new ClassFile(name, accessFlags, bytes);






2095             }

2096 
2097             private static int readInt(byte[] bytes, int offset) {
2098                 if ((offset+4) > bytes.length) {
2099                     throw new ClassFormatError("Invalid ClassFile structure");
2100                 }
2101                 return ((bytes[offset] & 0xFF) << 24)
2102                         | ((bytes[offset + 1] & 0xFF) << 16)
2103                         | ((bytes[offset + 2] & 0xFF) << 8)
2104                         | (bytes[offset + 3] & 0xFF);
2105             }
2106 
2107             private static int readUnsignedShort(byte[] bytes, int offset) {
2108                 if ((offset+2) > bytes.length) {
2109                     throw new ClassFormatError("Invalid ClassFile structure");
2110                 }
2111                 return ((bytes[offset] & 0xFF) << 8) | (bytes[offset + 1] & 0xFF);
2112             }
2113         }
2114

2117          * from the given bytes.
2118          *
2119          * Caller should make a defensive copy of the arguments if needed
2120          * before calling this factory method.
2121          *
2122          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code bytes} is not a class or interface or
2123          * {@bytes} denotes a class in a different package than the lookup class
2124          */
2125         private ClassDefiner makeClassDefiner(byte[] bytes) {
2126             ClassFile cf = ClassFile.newInstance(bytes, lookupClass().getPackageName());
2127             return new ClassDefiner(this, cf, STRONG_LOADER_LINK);

2184         /**
2185          * Returns a ClassDefiner that creates a {@code Class} object of a hidden class
2186          * from the given class file and options.
2187          *
2188          * @param cf ClassFile

2189          * @param options class options
2190          * @param accessVmAnnotations true to give the hidden class access to VM annotations
2191          */
2192         private ClassDefiner makeHiddenClassDefiner(ClassFile cf,
2193                                                     Set<ClassOption> options,
2194                                                     boolean accessVmAnnotations) {

2195             int flags = HIDDEN_CLASS | ClassOption.optionsToFlag(options);
2196             if (accessVmAnnotations | VM.isSystemDomainLoader(lookupClass.getClassLoader())) {
2197                 // jdk.internal.vm.annotations are permitted for classes
2198                 // defined to boot loader and platform loader
2199                 flags |= ACCESS_VM_ANNOTATIONS;
2200             }
2201 
2202             return new ClassDefiner(this, cf, flags);
2203         }

2205         static class ClassDefiner {
2206             private final Lookup lookup;
2207             private final String name;
2208             private final byte[] bytes;
2209             private final int classFlags;
2210 
2211             private ClassDefiner(Lookup lookup, ClassFile cf, int flags) {
2212                 assert ((flags & HIDDEN_CLASS) != 0 || (flags & STRONG_LOADER_LINK) == STRONG_LOADER_LINK);
2213                 this.lookup = lookup;
2214                 this.bytes = cf.bytes;
2215                 this.name = cf.name;
2216                 this.classFlags = flags;

2217             }
2218 
2219             String className() {
2220                 return name;
2221             }
2222 
2223             Class<?> defineClass(boolean initialize) {
2224                 return defineClass(initialize, null);
2225             }
2226 
2227             Lookup defineClassAsLookup(boolean initialize) {
2228                 Class<?> c = defineClass(initialize, null);
2229                 return new Lookup(c, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
2230             }
2231 
2232             /**
2233              * Defines the class of the given bytes and the given classData.
2234              * If {@code initialize} parameter is true, then the class will be initialized.
2235              *
2236              * @param initialize true if the class to be initialized
2237              * @param classData classData or null
2238              * @return the class
2239              *
2240              * @throws LinkageError linkage error
2241              */
2242             Class<?> defineClass(boolean initialize, Object classData) {
2243                 Class<?> lookupClass = lookup.lookupClass();
2244                 ClassLoader loader = lookupClass.getClassLoader();
2245                 ProtectionDomain pd = (loader != null) ? lookup.lookupClassProtectionDomain() : null;
2246                 Class<?> c = JLA.defineClass(loader, lookupClass, name, bytes, pd, initialize, classFlags, classData);
2247                 assert !isNestmate() || c.getNestHost() == lookupClass.getNestHost();
2248                 return c;
2249             }
2250 
2251             Lookup defineClassAsLookup(boolean initialize, Object classData) {
2252                 // initialize must be true if classData is non-null
2253                 assert classData == null || initialize == true;
2254                 Class<?> c = defineClass(initialize, classData);
2255                 return new Lookup(c, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
2256             }
2257 
2258             private boolean isNestmate() {
2259                 return (classFlags & NESTMATE_CLASS) != 0;
2260             }
2261         }
2262 
2263         private ProtectionDomain lookupClassProtectionDomain() {
2264             ProtectionDomain pd = cachedProtectionDomain;
2265             if (pd == null) {
2266                 cachedProtectionDomain = pd = JLA.protectionDomain(lookupClass);
2267             }
2268             return pd;
2269         }

2280         /** Version of lookup which is trusted minimally.
2281          *  It can only be used to create method handles to publicly accessible
2282          *  members in packages that are exported unconditionally.
2283          */
2284         static final Lookup PUBLIC_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, UNCONDITIONAL);

2288         private static void checkUnprivilegedlookupClass(Class<?> lookupClass) {
2289             String name = lookupClass.getName();
2290             if (name.startsWith("java.lang.invoke."))
2291                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal lookupClass: "+lookupClass);
2292         }
