2294         /**
2295          * Displays the name of the class from which lookups are to be made,
2296          * followed by "/" and the name of the {@linkplain #previousLookupClass()
2297          * previous lookup class} if present.
2298          * (The name is the one reported by {@link java.lang.Class#getName() Class.getName}.)
2299          * If there are restrictions on the access permitted to this lookup,
2300          * this is indicated by adding a suffix to the class name, consisting
2301          * of a slash and a keyword.  The keyword represents the strongest
2302          * allowed access, and is chosen as follows:
2303          * <ul>
2304          * <li>If no access is allowed, the suffix is "/noaccess".
2305          * <li>If only unconditional access is allowed, the suffix is "/publicLookup".
2306          * <li>If only public access to types in exported packages is allowed, the suffix is "/public".
2307          * <li>If only public and module access are allowed, the suffix is "/module".
2308          * <li>If public and package access are allowed, the suffix is "/package".
2309          * <li>If public, package, and private access are allowed, the suffix is "/private".
2310          * </ul>
2311          * If none of the above cases apply, it is the case that full access
2312          * (public, module, package, private, and protected) is allowed.
2313          * In this case, no suffix is added.
2314          * This is true only of an object obtained originally from
2315          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#lookup MethodHandles.lookup}.
2316          * Objects created by {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.Lookup#in Lookup.in}
2317          * always have restricted access, and will display a suffix.
2318          * <p>
2319          * (It may seem strange that protected access should be
2320          * stronger than private access.  Viewed independently from
2321          * package access, protected access is the first to be lost,
2322          * because it requires a direct subclass relationship between
2323          * caller and callee.)
2324          * @see #in
2325          *
2326          * @revised 9
2327          * @spec JPMS
2328          */
2329         @Override
2330         public String toString() {
2331             String cname = lookupClass.getName();
2332             if (prevLookupClass != null)
2333                 cname += "/" + prevLookupClass.getName();
2334             switch (allowedModes) {
2335             case 0:  // no privileges
2336                 return cname + "/noaccess";
2337             case UNCONDITIONAL:
2338                 return cname + "/publicLookup";
2339             case PUBLIC:
2340                 return cname + "/public";
2341             case PUBLIC|MODULE:
2342                 return cname + "/module";
2343             case PUBLIC|PACKAGE:
2344             case PUBLIC|MODULE|PACKAGE:
2345                 return cname + "/package";
2346             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~PROTECTED):
2347             case FULL_POWER_MODES & ~(PROTECTED|MODULE):
2348                 return cname + "/private";
2349             case FULL_POWER_MODES:
2350             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~MODULE):
2351                 return cname;
2352             case TRUSTED:
2353                 return "/trusted";  // internal only; not exported
2354             default:  // Should not happen, but it's a bitfield...
2355                 cname = cname + "/" + Integer.toHexString(allowedModes);
2356                 assert(false) : cname;
2357                 return cname;
2358             }
2359         }
2360 
2361         /**
2362          * Produces a method handle for a static method.
2363          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method.
2364          * (Since static methods do not take receivers, there is no
2365          * additional receiver argument inserted into the method handle type,
2366          * as there would be with {@link #findVirtual findVirtual} or {@link #findSpecial findSpecial}.)
2367          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2368          * <p>
2369          * The returned method handle will have
2370          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2371          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2372          * <p>
2373          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
2374          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2375          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2376          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2377 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2378 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2379 ...
2380 MethodHandle MH_asList = publicLookup().findStatic(Arrays.class,
2381   "asList", methodType(List.class, Object[].class));
2382 assertEquals("[x, y]", MH_asList.invoke("x", "y").toString());
2383          * }</pre></blockquote>
2384          * @param refc the class from which the method is accessed
2385          * @param name the name of the method
2386          * @param type the type of the method
2387          * @return the desired method handle
2388          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2389          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2390          *                                or if the method is not {@code static},
2391          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2392          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2393          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2394          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2395          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2396          */
2397         public MethodHandle findStatic(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2398             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeStatic, refc, name, type);
2399             return getDirectMethod(REF_invokeStatic, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2400         }
2401 
2402         /**
2403          * Produces a method handle for a virtual method.
2404          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2405          * with the receiver type (usually {@code refc}) prepended.
2406          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2407          * <p>
2408          * When called, the handle will treat the first argument as a receiver
2409          * and, for non-private methods, dispatch on the receiver's type to determine which method
2410          * implementation to enter.
2411          * For private methods the named method in {@code refc} will be invoked on the receiver.
2412          * (The dispatching action is identical with that performed by an
2413          * {@code invokevirtual} or {@code invokeinterface} instruction.)
2414          * <p>
2415          * The first argument will be of type {@code refc} if the lookup
2416          * class has full privileges to access the member.  Otherwise
2417          * the member must be {@code protected} and the first argument
2418          * will be restricted in type to the lookup class.
2419          * <p>
2420          * The returned method handle will have
2421          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2422          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2423          * <p>
2424          * Because of the general <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">equivalence</a> between {@code invokevirtual}
2425          * instructions and method handles produced by {@code findVirtual},
2426          * if the class is {@code MethodHandle} and the name string is
2427          * {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke}, the resulting
2428          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2429          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#exactInvoker MethodHandles.exactInvoker} or
2430          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#invoker MethodHandles.invoker}
2431          * with the same {@code type} argument.
2432          * <p>
2433          * If the class is {@code VarHandle} and the name string corresponds to
2434          * the name of a signature-polymorphic access mode method, the resulting
2435          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2436          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#varHandleInvoker} with
2437          * the access mode corresponding to the name string and with the same
2438          * {@code type} arguments.
2439          * <p>
2440          * <b>Example:</b>
2441          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2442 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2443 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2444 ...
2445 MethodHandle MH_concat = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2446   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
2447 MethodHandle MH_hashCode = publicLookup().findVirtual(Object.class,
2448   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2449 MethodHandle MH_hashCode_String = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2450   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2451 assertEquals("xy", (String) MH_concat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
2452 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode.invokeExact((Object)"xy"));
2453 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode_String.invokeExact("xy"));
2454 // interface method:
2455 MethodHandle MH_subSequence = publicLookup().findVirtual(CharSequence.class,
2456   "subSequence", methodType(CharSequence.class, int.class, int.class));
2457 assertEquals("def", MH_subSequence.invoke("abcdefghi", 3, 6).toString());
2458 // constructor "internal method" must be accessed differently:
2459 MethodType MT_newString = methodType(void.class); //()V for new String()
2460 try { assertEquals("impossible", lookup()
2461         .findVirtual(String.class, "<init>", MT_newString));
2462  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2463 MethodHandle MH_newString = publicLookup()
2464   .findConstructor(String.class, MT_newString);
2465 assertEquals("", (String) MH_newString.invokeExact());
2466          * }</pre></blockquote>
2467          *
2468          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2469          * @param name the name of the method
2470          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2471          * @return the desired method handle
2472          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2473          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2474          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2475          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2476          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2477          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2478          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2479          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2480          */
2481         public MethodHandle findVirtual(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2482             if (refc == MethodHandle.class) {
2483                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForMH(name, type);
2484                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2485             } else if (refc == VarHandle.class) {
2486                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForVH(name, type);
2487                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2488             }
2489             byte refKind = (refc.isInterface() ? REF_invokeInterface : REF_invokeVirtual);
2490             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(refKind, refc, name, type);
2491             return getDirectMethod(refKind, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2492         }
2493         private MethodHandle findVirtualForMH(String name, MethodType type) {
2494             // these names require special lookups because of the implicit MethodType argument
2495             if ("invoke".equals(name))
2496                 return invoker(type);
2497             if ("invokeExact".equals(name))
2498                 return exactInvoker(type);
2499             assert(!MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(name));
2500             return null;
2501         }
2502         private MethodHandle findVirtualForVH(String name, MethodType type) {
2503             try {
2504                 return varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode.valueFromMethodName(name), type);
2505             } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
2506                 return null;
2507             }
2508         }
2509 
2510         /**
2511          * Produces a method handle which creates an object and initializes it, using
2512          * the constructor of the specified type.
2513          * The parameter types of the method handle will be those of the constructor,
2514          * while the return type will be a reference to the constructor's class.
2515          * The constructor and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2516          * <p>
2517          * The requested type must have a return type of {@code void}.
2518          * (This is consistent with the JVM's treatment of constructor type descriptors.)
2519          * <p>
2520          * The returned method handle will have
2521          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2522          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2523          * <p>
2524          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
2525          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2526          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2527          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2528 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2529 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2530 ...
2531 MethodHandle MH_newArrayList = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2532   ArrayList.class, methodType(void.class, Collection.class));
2533 Collection orig = Arrays.asList("x", "y");
2534 Collection copy = (ArrayList) MH_newArrayList.invokeExact(orig);
2535 assert(orig != copy);
2536 assertEquals(orig, copy);
2537 // a variable-arity constructor:
2538 MethodHandle MH_newProcessBuilder = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2539   ProcessBuilder.class, methodType(void.class, String[].class));
2540 ProcessBuilder pb = (ProcessBuilder)
2541   MH_newProcessBuilder.invoke("x", "y", "z");
2542 assertEquals("[x, y, z]", pb.command().toString());
2543          * }</pre></blockquote>
2544          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2545          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted, and a void return type
2546          * @return the desired method handle
2547          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the constructor does not exist
2548          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
2549          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2550          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2551          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2552          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2553          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2554          */
2555         public MethodHandle findConstructor(Class<?> refc, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2556             if (refc.isArray()) {
2557                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("no constructor for array class: " + refc.getName());
2558             }
2559             String name = "<init>";
2560             MemberName ctor = resolveOrFail(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2561             return getDirectConstructor(refc, ctor);
2562         }
2563 
2564         /**
2565          * Looks up a class by name from the lookup context defined by this {@code Lookup} object,
2566          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if resolved</a> by an {@code ldc} instruction.
2567          * Such a resolution, as specified in JVMS 5.4.3.1 section, attempts to locate and load the class,
2568          * and then determines whether the class is accessible to this lookup object.
2569          * <p>
2570          * The lookup context here is determined by the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class},
2571          * its class loader, and the {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes}.
2572          *
2573          * @param targetName the fully qualified name of the class to be looked up.
2574          * @return the requested class.
2575          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2576          *                           <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2577          * @throws LinkageError if the linkage fails
2578          * @throws ClassNotFoundException if the class cannot be loaded by the lookup class' loader.
2579          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible, using the allowed access
2580          * modes.
2581          * @since 9
2582          * @jvms 5.4.3.1 Class and Interface Resolution
2583          */
2584         public Class<?> findClass(String targetName) throws ClassNotFoundException, IllegalAccessException {
2585             Class<?> targetClass = Class.forName(targetName, false, lookupClass.getClassLoader());
2586             return accessClass(targetClass);
2587         }
2588 
2589         /**
2590          * Determines if a class can be accessed from the lookup context defined by
2591          * this {@code Lookup} object. The static initializer of the class is not run.
2592          * <p>
2593          * If the {@code targetClass} is in the same module as the lookup class,
2594          * the lookup class is {@code LC} in module {@code M1} and
2595          * the previous lookup class is in module {@code M0} or
2596          * {@code null} if not present,
2597          * {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if one of the following is true:
2598          * <ul>
2599          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PRIVATE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2600          *     {@code LC} or other class in the same nest of {@code LC}.</li>
2601          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PACKAGE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2602          *     in the same runtime package of {@code LC}.</li>
2603          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #MODULE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2604          *     a public type in {@code M1}.</li>
2605          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PUBLIC} access, {@code targetClass} is
2606          *     a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} to at least  {@code M0}
2607          *     if the previous lookup class is present; otherwise, {@code targetClass}
2608          *     is a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} unconditionally.</li>
2609          * </ul>
2610          *
2611          * <p>
2612          * Otherwise, if this lookup has {@link #UNCONDITIONAL} access, this lookup
2613          * can access public types in all modules when the type is in a package
2614          * that is exported unconditionally.
2615          * <p>
2616          * Otherwise, the target class is in a different module from {@code lookupClass},
2617          * and if this lookup does not have {@code PUBLIC} access, {@code lookupClass}
2618          * is inaccessible.
2619          * <p>
2620          * Otherwise, if this lookup has no {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2621          * {@code M1} is the module containing {@code lookupClass} and
2622          * {@code M2} is the module containing {@code targetClass},
2623          * then {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if
2624          * <ul>
2625          * <li>{@code M1} reads {@code M2}, and
2626          * <li>{@code targetClass} is public and in a package exported by
2627          *     {@code M2} at least to {@code M1}.
2628          * </ul>
2629          * <p>
2630          * Otherwise, if this lookup has a {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2631          * {@code M1} and {@code M2} are as before, and {@code M0} is the module
2632          * containing the previous lookup class, then {@code targetClass} is accessible
2633          * if and only if one of the following is true:
2634          * <ul>
2635          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M0} and {@code M1}
2636          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M0} and the type is
2637          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M1}.
2638          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M1} and {@code M0}
2639          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M1} and the type is
2640          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M0}.
2641          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in a third module {@code M2} and both {@code M0}
2642          *     and {@code M1} reads {@code M2} and the type is in a package
2643          *     that is exported to at least both {@code M0} and {@code M2}.
2644          * </ul>
2645          * <p>
2646          * Otherwise, {@code targetClass} is not accessible.
2647          *
2648          * @param targetClass the class to be access-checked
2649          * @return the class that has been access-checked
2650          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible from the lookup class
2651          * and previous lookup class, if present, using the allowed access modes.
2652          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2653          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2654          * @since 9
2655          * @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
2656          */
2657         public Class<?> accessClass(Class<?> targetClass) throws IllegalAccessException {
2658             if (!VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(targetClass, lookupClass, prevLookupClass, allowedModes)) {
2659                 throw new MemberName(targetClass).makeAccessException("access violation", this);
2660             }
2661             checkSecurityManager(targetClass, null);
2662             return targetClass;
2663         }
2664 
2665         /**
2666          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a virtual method.
2667          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
2668          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
2669          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
2670          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2671          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
2672          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
2673          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible
2674          * to the lookup object.
2675          * <p>
2676          * Before method resolution,
2677          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
2678          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
2679          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
2680          * privileges, the access fails.
2681          * <p>
2682          * The returned method handle will have
2683          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2684          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2685          * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
2686          * <em>(Note:  JVM internal methods named {@code "<init>"} are not visible to this API,
2687          * even though the {@code invokespecial} instruction can refer to them
2688          * in special circumstances.  Use {@link #findConstructor findConstructor}
2689          * to access instance initialization methods in a safe manner.)</em>
2690          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2691          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2692 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2693 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2694 ...
2695 static class Listie extends ArrayList {
2696   public String toString() { return "[wee Listie]"; }
2697   static Lookup lookup() { return MethodHandles.lookup(); }
2698 }
2699 ...
2700 // no access to constructor via invokeSpecial:
2701 MethodHandle MH_newListie = Listie.lookup()
2702   .findConstructor(Listie.class, methodType(void.class));
2703 Listie l = (Listie) MH_newListie.invokeExact();
2704 try { assertEquals("impossible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2705         Listie.class, "<init>", methodType(void.class), Listie.class));
2706  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2707 // access to super and self methods via invokeSpecial:
2708 MethodHandle MH_super = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2709   ArrayList.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2710 MethodHandle MH_this = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2711   Listie.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2712 MethodHandle MH_duper = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2713   Object.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2714 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_super.invokeExact(l));
2715 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(l));
2716 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_duper.invokeExact(l)); // ArrayList method
2717 try { assertEquals("inaccessible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2718         String.class, "toString", methodType(String.class), Listie.class));
2719  } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) { } // OK
2720 Listie subl = new Listie() { public String toString() { return "[subclass]"; } };
2721 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(subl)); // Listie method
2722          * }</pre></blockquote>
2723          *
2724          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2725          * @param name the name of the method (which must not be "&lt;init&gt;")
2726          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2727          * @param specialCaller the proposed calling class to perform the {@code invokespecial}
2728          * @return the desired method handle
2729          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2730          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2731          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2732          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2733          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2734          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2735          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2736          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2737          */
2738         public MethodHandle findSpecial(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type,
2739                                         Class<?> specialCaller) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2740             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, refc);
2741             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
2742             MemberName method = specialLookup.resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2743             return specialLookup.getDirectMethod(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2744         }
2745 
2746         /**
2747          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a non-static field.
2748          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2749          * value type.
2750          * The method handle's single argument will be the instance containing
2751          * the field.
2752          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2753          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2754          * @param name the field's name
2755          * @param type the field's type
2756          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2757          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2758          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2759          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2760          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2761          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2762          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2763          */
2764         public MethodHandle findGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2765             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, refc, name, type);
2766             return getDirectField(REF_getField, refc, field);
2767         }
2768 
2769         /**
2770          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a non-static field.
2771          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2772          * The method handle will take two arguments, the instance containing
2773          * the field, and the value to be stored.
2774          * The second argument will be of the field's value type.
2775          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2776          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2777          * @param name the field's name
2778          * @param type the field's type
2779          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2780          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2781          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2782          *                                or {@code final}
2783          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2784          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2785          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2786          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2787          */
2788         public MethodHandle findSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2789             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, refc, name, type);
2790             return getDirectField(REF_putField, refc, field);
2791         }
2792 
2793         /**
2794          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a non-static field {@code name}
2795          * of type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code recv}.
2796          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has one
2797          * coordinate type, {@code recv}.
2798          * <p>
2799          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2800          * class.
2801          * <p>
2802          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2803          * the following conditions:
2804          * <ul>
2805          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2806          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2807          *     modes are unsupported.
2808          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2809          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2810          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
2811          *     access modes are unsupported.
2812          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2813          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2814          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2815          *     unsupported.
2816          * </ul>
2817          * <p>
2818          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2819          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2820          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2821          * access modes.
2822          * <p>
2823          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2824          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2825          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2826          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2827          * @apiNote
2828          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2829          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2830          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2831          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2832          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2833          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2834          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2835          * unexpectedly fail.
2836          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2837          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2838          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2839          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2840          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2841          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2842          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2843          * details).
2844          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2845          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2846          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2847          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2848          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2849          * @param recv the receiver class, of type {@code R}, that declares the
2850          * non-static field
2851          * @param name the field's name
2852          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2853          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields.
2854          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2855          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2856          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2857          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2858          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2859          * @since 9
2860          */
2861         public VarHandle findVarHandle(Class<?> recv, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2862             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, recv, name, type);
2863             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, recv, name, type);
2864             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getField, REF_putField, recv, getField, putField);
2865         }
2866 
2867         /**
2868          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a static field.
2869          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2870          * value type.
2871          * The method handle will take no arguments.
2872          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2873          * <p>
2874          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2875          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2876          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2877          * @param name the field's name
2878          * @param type the field's type
2879          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2880          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2881          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2882          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2883          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2884          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2885          */
2886         public MethodHandle findStaticGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2887             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, refc, name, type);
2888             return getDirectField(REF_getStatic, refc, field);
2889         }
2890 
2891         /**
2892          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a static field.
2893          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2894          * The method handle will take a single
2895          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
2896          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2897          * <p>
2898          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2899          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2900          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2901          * @param name the field's name
2902          * @param type the field's type
2903          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2904          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2905          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2906          *                                or is {@code final}
2907          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2908          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2909          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2910          */
2911         public MethodHandle findStaticSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2912             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, refc, name, type);
2913             return getDirectField(REF_putStatic, refc, field);
2914         }
2915 
2916         /**
2917          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a static field {@code name} of
2918          * type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code decl}.
2919          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has no
2920          * coordinate types.
2921          * <p>
2922          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2923          * class.
2924          * <p>
2925          * If the returned VarHandle is operated on, the declaring class will be
2926          * initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2927          * <p>
2928          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2929          * the following conditions:
2930          * <ul>
2931          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2932          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2933          *     modes are unsupported.
2934          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2935          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2936          *     {@code float}, or {@code double}, then numeric atomic update
2937          *     access modes are unsupported.
2938          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2939          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2940          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2941          *     unsupported.
2942          * </ul>
2943          * <p>
2944          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2945          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2946          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2947          * access modes.
2948          * <p>
2949          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2950          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2951          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2952          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2953          * @apiNote
2954          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2955          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2956          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2957          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2958          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2959          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2960          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2961          * unexpectedly fail.
2962          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2963          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2964          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2965          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2966          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2967          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2968          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2969          * details).
2970          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2971          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2972          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2973          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2974          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2975          * @param decl the class that declares the static field
2976          * @param name the field's name
2977          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2978          * @return a VarHandle giving access to a static field
2979          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2980          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2981          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2982          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2983          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2984          * @since 9
2985          */
2986         public VarHandle findStaticVarHandle(Class<?> decl, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2987             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, decl, name, type);
2988             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, decl, name, type);
2989             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getStatic, REF_putStatic, decl, getField, putField);
2990         }
2991 
2992         /**
2993          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a non-static method.
2994          * The receiver must have a supertype {@code defc} in which a method
2995          * of the given name and type is accessible to the lookup class.
2996          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2997          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2998          * without any insertion of an additional receiver parameter.
2999          * The given receiver will be bound into the method handle,
3000          * so that every call to the method handle will invoke the
3001          * requested method on the given receiver.
3002          * <p>
3003          * The returned method handle will have
3004          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3005          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set
3006          * <em>and</em> the trailing array argument is not the only argument.
3007          * (If the trailing array argument is the only argument,
3008          * the given receiver value will be bound to it.)
3009          * <p>
3010          * This is almost equivalent to the following code, with some differences noted below:
3011          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3012 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
3013 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
3014 ...
3015 MethodHandle mh0 = lookup().findVirtual(defc, name, type);
3016 MethodHandle mh1 = mh0.bindTo(receiver);
3017 mh1 = mh1.withVarargs(mh0.isVarargsCollector());
3018 return mh1;
3019          * }</pre></blockquote>
3020          * where {@code defc} is either {@code receiver.getClass()} or a super
3021          * type of that class, in which the requested method is accessible
3022          * to the lookup class.
3023          * (Unlike {@code bind}, {@code bindTo} does not preserve variable arity.
3024          * Also, {@code bindTo} may throw a {@code ClassCastException} in instances where {@code bind} would
3025          * throw an {@code IllegalAccessException}, as in the case where the member is {@code protected} and
3026          * the receiver is restricted by {@code findVirtual} to the lookup class.)
3027          * @param receiver the object from which the method is accessed
3028          * @param name the name of the method
3029          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
3030          * @return the desired method handle
3031          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
3032          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3033          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3034          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3035          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3036          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3037          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3038          * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
3039          * @see #findVirtual
3040          */
3041         public MethodHandle bind(Object receiver, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3042             Class<? extends Object> refc = receiver.getClass(); // may get NPE
3043             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
3044             MethodHandle mh = getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3045             if (!mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().isAssignableFrom(receiver.getClass())) {
3046                 throw new IllegalAccessException("The restricted defining class " +
3047                                                  mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().getName() +
3048                                                  " is not assignable from receiver class " +
3049                                                  receiver.getClass().getName());
3050             }
3051             return mh.bindArgumentL(0, receiver).setVarargs(method);
3052         }
3053 
3054         /**
3055          * Makes a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3056          * to <i>m</i>, if the lookup class has permission.
3057          * If <i>m</i> is non-static, the receiver argument is treated as an initial argument.
3058          * If <i>m</i> is virtual, overriding is respected on every call.
3059          * Unlike the Core Reflection API, exceptions are <em>not</em> wrapped.
3060          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3061          * with the receiver type prepended (but only if it is non-static).
3062          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3063          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3064          * If <i>m</i> is not public, do not share the resulting handle with untrusted parties.
3065          * <p>
3066          * The returned method handle will have
3067          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3068          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3069          * <p>
3070          * If <i>m</i> is static, and
3071          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
3072          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3073          * @param m the reflected method
3074          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3075          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3076          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3077          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3078          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3079          */
3080         public MethodHandle unreflect(Method m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3081             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == MethodHandle.class) {
3082                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForMH(m);
3083                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3084             }
3085             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == VarHandle.class) {
3086                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForVH(m);
3087                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3088             }
3089             MemberName method = new MemberName(m);
3090             byte refKind = method.getReferenceKind();
3091             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial)
3092                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3093             assert(method.isMethod());
3094             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3095             Lookup lookup = m.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3096             return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3097         }
3098         private MethodHandle unreflectForMH(Method m) {
3099             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3100             if (MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(m.getName()))
3101                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeMethodHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3102             return null;
3103         }
3104         private MethodHandle unreflectForVH(Method m) {
3105             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3106             if (MemberName.isVarHandleMethodInvokeName(m.getName()))
3107                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeVarHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3108             return null;
3109         }
3110 
3111         /**
3112          * Produces a method handle for a reflected method.
3113          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
3114          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
3115          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
3116          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3117          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
3118          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
3119          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3120          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class,
3121          * as if {@code invokespecial} instruction were being linked.
3122          * <p>
3123          * Before method resolution,
3124          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
3125          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
3126          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
3127          * privileges, the access fails.
3128          * <p>
3129          * The returned method handle will have
3130          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3131          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3132          * @param m the reflected method
3133          * @param specialCaller the class nominally calling the method
3134          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3135          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3136          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
3137          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3138          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3139          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3140          */
3141         public MethodHandle unreflectSpecial(Method m, Class<?> specialCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3142             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, m.getDeclaringClass());
3143             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
3144             MemberName method = new MemberName(m, true);
3145             assert(method.isMethod());
3146             // ignore m.isAccessible:  this is a new kind of access
3147             return specialLookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(REF_invokeSpecial, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3148         }
3149 
3150         /**
3151          * Produces a method handle for a reflected constructor.
3152          * The type of the method handle will be that of the constructor,
3153          * with the return type changed to the declaring class.
3154          * The method handle will perform a {@code newInstance} operation,
3155          * creating a new instance of the constructor's class on the
3156          * arguments passed to the method handle.
3157          * <p>
3158          * If the constructor's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3159          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3160          * <p>
3161          * The returned method handle will have
3162          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3163          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3164          * <p>
3165          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
3166          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3167          * @param c the reflected constructor
3168          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected constructor
3169          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3170          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3171          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3172          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3173          */
3174         public MethodHandle unreflectConstructor(Constructor<?> c) throws IllegalAccessException {
3175             MemberName ctor = new MemberName(c);
3176             assert(ctor.isConstructor());
3177             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3178             Lookup lookup = c.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3179             return lookup.getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor);
3180         }

3182         /**
3183          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a reflected field.
3184          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
3185          * value type.
3186          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take no arguments.
3187          * Otherwise, its single argument will be the instance containing
3188          * the field.
3189          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3190          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3191          * <p>
3192          * If the field is static, and
3193          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3194          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3195          * @param f the reflected field
3196          * @return a method handle which can load values from the reflected field
3197          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3198          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3199          */
3200         public MethodHandle unreflectGetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3201             return unreflectField(f, false);
3202         }
3203 
3204         /**
3205          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a reflected field.
3206          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3207          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take a single
3208          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
3209          * Otherwise, the two arguments will be the instance containing
3210          * the field, and the value to be stored.
3211          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3212          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3213          * <p>
3214          * If the field is {@code final}, write access will not be
3215          * allowed and access checking will fail, except under certain
3216          * narrow circumstances documented for {@link Field#set Field.set}.
3217          * A method handle is returned only if a corresponding call to
3218          * the {@code Field} object's {@code set} method could return
3219          * normally.  In particular, fields which are both {@code static}
3220          * and {@code final} may never be set.
3221          * <p>
3222          * If the field is {@code static}, and
3223          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3224          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3225          * @param f the reflected field
3226          * @return a method handle which can store values into the reflected field
3227          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3228          *         or if the field is {@code final} and write access
3229          *         is not enabled on the {@code Field} object
3230          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3231          */
3232         public MethodHandle unreflectSetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3233             return unreflectField(f, true);
3234         }
3235 
3236         private MethodHandle unreflectField(Field f, boolean isSetter) throws IllegalAccessException {
3237             MemberName field = new MemberName(f, isSetter);
3238             if (isSetter && field.isFinal()) {
3239                 if (field.isStatic()) {
3240                     throw field.makeAccessException("static final field has no write access", this);
3241                 } else if (field.getDeclaringClass().isHidden()){
3242                     throw field.makeAccessException("final field in a hidden class has no write access", this);
3243                 }
3244             }
3245             assert(isSetter
3246                     ? MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(field.getReferenceKind())
3247                     : MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(field.getReferenceKind()));
3248             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3249             Lookup lookup = f.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3250             return lookup.getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(field.getReferenceKind(), f.getDeclaringClass(), field);
3251         }
3252 
3253         /**
3254          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a reflected field {@code f}
3255          * of type {@code T} declared in a class of type {@code R}.
3256          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code T}.
3257          * If the field is non-static the VarHandle has one coordinate type,
3258          * {@code R}.  Otherwise, the field is static, and the VarHandle has no
3259          * coordinate types.
3260          * <p>
3261          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
3262          * class, regardless of the value of the field's {@code accessible}
3263          * flag.
3264          * <p>
3265          * If the field is static, and if the returned VarHandle is operated
3266          * on, the field's declaring class will be initialized, if it has not
3267          * already been initialized.
3268          * <p>
3269          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3270          * the following conditions:
3271          * <ul>
3272          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
3273          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
3274          *     modes are unsupported.
3275          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
3276          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3277          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
3278          *     access modes are unsupported.
3279          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3280          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3281          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3282          *     unsupported.
3283          * </ul>
3284          * <p>
3285          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
3286          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
3287          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3288          * access modes.
3289          * <p>
3290          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3291          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3292          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3293          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3294          * @apiNote
3295          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3296          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3297          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3298          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3299          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3300          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3301          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3302          * unexpectedly fail.
3303          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3304          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3305          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3306          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3307          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3308          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3309          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3310          * details).
3311          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3312          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3313          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3314          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3315          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3316          * @param f the reflected field, with a field of type {@code T}, and
3317          * a declaring class of type {@code R}
3318          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields or a static
3319          * field
3320          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3321          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3322          * @since 9
3323          */
3324         public VarHandle unreflectVarHandle(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3325             MemberName getField = new MemberName(f, false);
3326             MemberName putField = new MemberName(f, true);
3327             return getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(getField.getReferenceKind(), putField.getReferenceKind(),
3328                                                       f.getDeclaringClass(), getField, putField);
3329         }
3330 
3331         /**
3332          * Cracks a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3333          * created by this lookup object or a similar one.
3334          * Security and access checks are performed to ensure that this lookup object
3335          * is capable of reproducing the target method handle.
3336          * This means that the cracking may fail if target is a direct method handle
3337          * but was created by an unrelated lookup object.
3338          * This can happen if the method handle is <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#callsens">caller sensitive</a>
3339          * and was created by a lookup object for a different class.
3340          * @param target a direct method handle to crack into symbolic reference components
3341          * @return a symbolic reference which can be used to reconstruct this method handle from this lookup object
3342          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3343          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3344          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the target is not a direct method handle or if access checking fails
3345          * @throws    NullPointerException if the target is {@code null}
3346          * @see MethodHandleInfo
3347          * @since 1.8
3348          */
3349         public MethodHandleInfo revealDirect(MethodHandle target) {
3350             if (!target.isCrackable()) {
3351                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("not a direct method handle");
3352             }
3353             MemberName member = target.internalMemberName();
3354             Class<?> defc = member.getDeclaringClass();
3355             byte refKind = member.getReferenceKind();
3356             assert(MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind));
3357             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial && !target.isInvokeSpecial())
3358                 // Devirtualized method invocation is usually formally virtual.
3359                 // To avoid creating extra MemberName objects for this common case,
3360                 // we encode this extra degree of freedom using MH.isInvokeSpecial.
3361                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3362             if (refKind == REF_invokeVirtual && defc.isInterface())
3363                 // Symbolic reference is through interface but resolves to Object method (toString, etc.)
3364                 refKind = REF_invokeInterface;
3365             // Check SM permissions and member access before cracking.
3366             try {
3367                 checkAccess(refKind, defc, member);
3368                 checkSecurityManager(defc, member);
3369             } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) {
3370                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
3371             }
3372             if (allowedModes != TRUSTED && member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3373                 Class<?> callerClass = target.internalCallerClass();
3374                 if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess() || callerClass != lookupClass())
3375                     throw new IllegalArgumentException("method handle is caller sensitive: "+callerClass);
3376             }
3377             // Produce the handle to the results.
3378             return new InfoFromMemberName(this, member, refKind);
3379         }
3380 
3381         /// Helper methods, all package-private.
3382 
3383         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3384             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3385             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3386             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3387             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3388                                             NoSuchFieldException.class);
3389         }
3390 
3391         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3392             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3393             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3394             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3395             checkMethodName(refKind, name);  // NPE check on name
3396             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3397                                             NoSuchMethodException.class);
3398         }
3399 
3400         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, MemberName member) throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3401             checkSymbolicClass(member.getDeclaringClass());  // do this before attempting to resolve
3402             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3403             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3404             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull(),
3405                                             ReflectiveOperationException.class);
3406         }
3407 
3408         MemberName resolveOrNull(byte refKind, MemberName member) {
3409             // do this before attempting to resolve
3410             if (!isClassAccessible(member.getDeclaringClass())) {
3411                 return null;
3412             }
3413             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3414             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3415             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull());
3416         }
3417 
3418         void checkSymbolicClass(Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3419             if (!isClassAccessible(refc)) {
3420                 throw new MemberName(refc).makeAccessException("symbolic reference class is not accessible", this);
3421             }
3422         }
3423 
3424         boolean isClassAccessible(Class<?> refc) {
3425             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3426             Class<?> caller = lookupClassOrNull();
3427             return caller == null || VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, caller, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
3428         }
3429 
3430         /** Check name for an illegal leading "&lt;" character. */
3431         void checkMethodName(byte refKind, String name) throws NoSuchMethodException {
3432             if (name.startsWith("<") && refKind != REF_newInvokeSpecial)
3433                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: "+name);
3434         }
