3436 
3437         /**
3438          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3439          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3440          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3441          */
3442         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3443             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3444                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3445                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3446             }
3447             return this;
3448         }
3449 
3450         /**
3451          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3452          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3453          *
3454          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3455          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3456          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3457          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3458          * @since 9
3459          */
3460         @Deprecated(since="14")
3461         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3462             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3463         }
3464 
3465         /**
3466          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3467          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3468          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3469          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3470          *
3471          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3472          * @since 14
3473          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3474          */
3475         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3476             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3477         }
3478 
3479         /**
3480          * Perform necessary <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3481          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3482          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3483          */
3484         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3485             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3486 
3487             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3488             if (smgr == null)  return;
3489 
3490             // Step 1:
3491             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3492             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3493                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3494                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3495             }
3496 
3497             if (m == null) {  // findClass or accessClass
3498                 // Step 2b:
3499                 if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3500                     smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3501                 }
3502                 return;
3503             }
3504 
3505             // Step 2a:
3506             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3507             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3508                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3509             }
3510 
3511             // Step 3:
3512             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3513             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3514                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3515             }
3516         }
3517 
3518         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3519             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3520             String message;
3521             if (m.isConstructor())
3522                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3523             else if (!m.isMethod())
3524                 message = "expected a method";
3525             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3526                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3527             else
3528                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3529             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3530         }
3531 
3532         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3533             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3534             String message;
3535             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3536                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3537             else
3538                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3539             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3540         }
3541 
3542         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3543         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3544             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3545                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3546                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3547             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3548             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3549             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3550             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3551                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3552                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3553                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3554                     refc.isArray()) {
3555                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3556                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3557                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3558                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3559                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3560                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3561                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3562                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3563                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3564                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3565                 // requested array type.
3566                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3567                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3568                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3569             }
3570             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3571                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3572                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3573             }
3574             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3575                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3576                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3577             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3578             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3579                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3580                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3581                     return;
3582             } else {
3583                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3584                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3585                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3586                     return;
3587             }
3588             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3589         }
3590 
3591         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3592             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3593             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3594             // check the class first:
3595             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3596                                (defc == refc ||
3597                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3598             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3599                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3600                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3601                            (defc == refc ||
3602                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3603             }
3604             if (!classOK)
3605                 return "class is not public";
3606             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3607                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3608             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3609                 return "member is private";
3610             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3611                 return "member is protected";
3612             return "member is private to package";
3613         }
3614 
3615         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3616             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3617             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3618             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3619                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3620                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3621                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3622                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3623                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3624         }
3625 
3626         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3627             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3628             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3629             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3630                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3631                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3632                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3633                 return false;
3634             return true;
3635         }
3636         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3637             assert(!method.isStatic());
3638             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3639             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3640                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3641             }
3642             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3643             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3644             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3645             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3646             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3647             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3648         }
3649 
3650         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3651         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3652             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3653             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3654             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3655         }
3656         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3657         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3658             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3659             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3660             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3661         }
3662         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3663         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3664             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3665             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3666             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3667         }
3668         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3669         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3670                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3671                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3672                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3673             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3674             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3675             if (checkSecurity)
3676                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3677             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3678 
3679             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3680                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3681                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3682                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3683                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3684                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3685 
3686                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3687                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3688                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3689                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3690                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3691                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3692                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3693                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3694                 MemberName m2;
3695                 do {
3696                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3697                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3698                                         method.getName(),
3699                                         method.getMethodType(),
3700                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3701                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3702                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3703                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3704                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3705                 method = m2;
3706                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3707                 // redo basic checks
3708                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3709             }
3710             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3711             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3712             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3713             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3714                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3715                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3716             }
3717             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3718             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3719             return mh;
3720         }
3721         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3722                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3723             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3724                 return mh;
3725 
3726             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3727             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3728             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3729                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3730 
3731             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3732             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3733             return cbmh;
3734         }
3735 
3736         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3737         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3738             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3739             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3740         }
3741         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3742         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3743             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3744             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3745         }
3746         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3747         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3748                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3749             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3750             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3751             if (checkSecurity)
3752                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3753             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3754             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3755                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3756             if (doRestrict)
3757                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3758             return dmh;
3759         }
3760         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3761                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3762                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3763             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3764             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3765         }
3766         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3767                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3768                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3769             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3770             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3771         }
3772         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3773                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3774                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3775             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3776             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3777             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3778             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3779 
3780             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3781             if (checkSecurity)
3782                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3783 
3784             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3785                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3786                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3787                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3788                 // only required for non-final fields
3789                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3790                 if (checkSecurity)
3791                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3792             }
3793 
3794             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3795                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3796             if (doRestrict) {
3797                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3798                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3799                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3800                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3801                 }
3802                 refc = lookupClass();
3803             }
3804             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3805                                              this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.getDeclaringClass().isHidden());
3806         }
3807         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3808         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3809             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3810             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3811         }
3812         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3813         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3814             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3815             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3816         }
3817         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3818         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3819                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3820             assert(ctor.isConstructor());
3821             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3822             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3823             if (checkSecurity)
3824                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3825             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3826             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3827         }
3828 
3829         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3830          */
3831         /*non-public*/
3832         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3833                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3834             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3835                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3836             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3837             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3838             if (mh != null) {
3839                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3840                 return mh;
3841             }
3842             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3843                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3844                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3845                 if (mh != null) {
3846                     return mh;
3847                 }
3848             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3849                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3850                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3851                 if (mh != null) {
3852                     return mh;
3853                 }
3854             }
3855             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3856             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3857             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3858                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3859                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3860                 if (key != null) {
3861                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3862                 }
3863                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3864                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3865                 }
3866             }
3867             return mh;
3868         }
3869         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3870             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3871                 return false;
3872             }
3873             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3874                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3875                     !member.isPublic() ||
3876                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3877                 return false;
3878             }
3879             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3880             if (loader != null) {
3881                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3882                 boolean found = false;
3883                 while (sysl != null) {
3884                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3885                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3886                 }
3887                 if (!found) {
3888                     return false;
3889                 }
3890             }
3891             try {
3892                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3893                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3894                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3895                     return false;
3896                 }
3897                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3898             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3899                 return false;
3900             }
3901             return true;
3902         }
3903         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3904                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3905             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3906                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3907             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3908                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3909             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3910                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3911             }
3912             // oops
3913             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3914         }
3915 
3916         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3917     }
3918 
3919     /**
3920      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3921      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3922      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3923      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
3924      *
3925      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
3926      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
3927      *
3928      * @param arrayClass an array type
3929      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
3930      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3931      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
3932      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
3933      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
3934      * @since 9
3935      */
3936     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3937         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
3938             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
3939         }
3940         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
3941                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
3942         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
3943     }
3944 
3945     /**
3946      * Produces a method handle returning the length of an array,
3947      * as if by the {@code arraylength} bytecode.
3948      * The type of the method handle will have {@code int} as return type,
3949      * and its sole argument will be the array type.
3950      *
3951      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a {@code null}
3952      * array reference, a {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown.
3953      *
3954      * @param arrayClass an array type
3955      * @return a method handle which can retrieve the length of an array of the given array type
3956      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3957      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3958      * @jvms 6.5 {@code arraylength} Instruction
3959      * @since 9
3960      */
3961     public static MethodHandle arrayLength(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3962         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.LENGTH);
3963     }
3964 
3965     /**
3966      * Produces a method handle giving read access to elements of an array,
3967      * as if by the {@code aaload} bytecode.
3968      * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the array's
3969      * element type.  Its first argument will be the array type,
3970      * and the second will be {@code int}.
3971      *
3972      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3973      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3974      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3975      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3976      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3977      * the length of the array.
3978      *
3979      * @param arrayClass an array type
3980      * @return a method handle which can load values from the given array type
3981      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3982      * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3983      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aaload} Instruction
3984      */
3985     public static MethodHandle arrayElementGetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3986         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.GET);
3987     }
3988 
3989     /**
3990      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
3991      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
3992      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3993      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
3994      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
3995      *
3996      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3997      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3998      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3999      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4000      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4001      * the length of the array.
4002      *
4003      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
4004      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
4005      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4006      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4007      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
4008      */
4009     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4010         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
4011     }
4012 
4013     /**
4014      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
4015      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
4016      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4017      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4018      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
4019      * <p>
4020      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
4021      * the following conditions:
4022      * <ul>
4023      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
4024      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
4025      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
4026      *     modes are unsupported.
4027      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code boolean},
4028      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
4029      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
4030      *     unsupported.
4031      * </ul>
4032      * <p>
4033      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
4034      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
4035      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4036      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4037      *
4038      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
4039      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4040      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4041      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4042      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4043      * the length of the array.
4044      *
4045      * @apiNote
4046      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
4047      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
4048      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
4049      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
4050      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
4051      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
4052      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
4053      * unexpectedly fail.
4054      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
4055      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
4056      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
4057      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
4058      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
4059      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
4060      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
4061      * details).
4062      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
4063      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4064      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4065      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4066      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4067      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4068      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4069      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4070      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4071      * @since 9
4072      */
4073     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4074         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4075     }
4076 
4077     /**
4078      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4079      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4080      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4081      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4082      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4083      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4084      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4085      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4086      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4087      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4088      * <p>
4089      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4090      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4091      * {@code double}.
4092      * <p>
4093      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4094      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4095      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4096      * of {@code T}.
4097      * <p>
4098      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4099      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4100      * with the array and index.
4101      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4102      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4103      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4104      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4105      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4106      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4107      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4108      * <ul>
4109      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4110      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4111      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4112      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4113      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4114      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4115      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4116      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4117      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4118      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4119      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4120      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4121      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4122      * </ul>
4123      * <p>
4124      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4125      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4126      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4127      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4128      * <pre>{@code
4129      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4130      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4131      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4132      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4133      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4134      * }</pre>
4135      * <p>
4136      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4137      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4138      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4139      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4140      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4141      * type {@code T}
4142      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4143      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4144      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4145      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4146      * array class
4147      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4148      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4149      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4150      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4151      * @since 9
4152      */
4153     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4154                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4155         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4156         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4157                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4158     }
4159 
4160     /**
4161      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4162      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4163      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4164      * {@code long[]}.
4165      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4166      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4167      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4168      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4169      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4170      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4171      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4172      * <p>
4173      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4174      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4175      * {@code double}.
4176      * <p>
4177      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4178      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4179      * <p>
4180      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4181      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4182      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4183      * {@code T}.
4184      * <p>
4185      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4186      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4187      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4188      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4189      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4190      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4191      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4192      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4193      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4194      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4195      * <ul>
4196      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4197      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4198      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4199      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4200      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4201      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4202      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4203      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4204      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4205      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4206      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4207      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4208      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4209      * </ul>
4210      * <p>
4211      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4212      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4213      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4214      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4215      * <pre>{@code
4216      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4217      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4218      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4219      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4220      * }</pre>
4221      * <p>
4222      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4223      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4224      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4225      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4226      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4227      * type {@code T}
4228      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4229      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4230      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4231      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4232      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4233      * array class
4234      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4235      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4236      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4237      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4238      * @since 9
4239      */
4240     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4241                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4242         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4243         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4244                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4245     }
4246 
4247 
4248     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4249 
4250     /**
4251      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4252      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4253      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4254      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4255      * arguments:
4256      * <ul>
4257      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4258      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4259      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4260      * </ul>
4261      * <p>
4262      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4263      * the indicated {@code type}.
4264      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4265      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4266      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4267      * <p>
4268      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4269      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4270      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4271      * the final parameter.
4272      * <p>
4273      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4274      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4275      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4276      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4277      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4278      * <p>
4279      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4280      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4281 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4282 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4283 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4284 return invoker;
4285      * }</pre></blockquote>
4286      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4287      * @param type the desired target type
4288      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4289      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4290      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4291      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4292      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4293      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4294      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4295      */
4296     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4297         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4298             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4299         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4300         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4301     }
4302 
4303     /**
4304      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4305      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4306      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4307      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4308      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4309      * <p>
4310      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4311      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4312      *
4313      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4314      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4315      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4316      * of unknown types.
4317      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4318      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4319      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4320      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4321      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4322      * is unknown.)
4323      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4324      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4325      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4326      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4327      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4328      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4329      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4330      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4331      * <p>
4332      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4333      * @param type the desired target type
4334      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4335      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4336      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4337      */
4338     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4339         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4340     }
4341 
4342     /**
4343      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4344      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4345      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4346      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4347      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4348      * <p>
4349      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4350      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4351      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4352      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4353      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4354      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4355      * <p>
4356      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4357      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4358      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4359      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4360      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4361      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4362      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4363      * of the same arity as the general type.
4364      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4365      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4366      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4367      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4368      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4369      * <p>
4370      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4371      * @param type the desired target type
4372      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4373      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4374      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4375      */
4376     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4377         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4378     }

4380     /**
4381      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4382      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4383      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4384      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the

4391      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.

4394     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {

4399      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4400      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4401      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4402      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4403      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4404      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4405      * <p>
4406      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the

4430 
4431      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4432 
4433     /**
4434      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4435      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4436      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4437      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4438      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4439      * <p>
4440      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4441      * <p>
4442      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4443      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4444      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4445      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4446      * <ul>
4447      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4448      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4449      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4450      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4451      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4452      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4453      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4454      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4455      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4456      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4457      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4458      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4459      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4460      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4461      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4462      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4463      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4464      *     the low-order bit.
4465      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4466      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4467      * </ul>
4468      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4469      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4470      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4471      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4472      *           necessary return value conversions
4473      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4474      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4475      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4476      */
4477     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4478         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4479         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4480         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4481         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4482         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4483             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4484         }
4485         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4486     }
4487 
4488     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4489         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4490             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4491         }
4492     }
4493 
4494     /**
4495      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4496      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4497      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4498      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4499      * <p>
4500      * The given array controls the reordering.
4501      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4502      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
4503      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4504      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4505      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4506      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4507      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4508      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4509      * <p>
4510      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4511      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4512      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4513      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4514      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4515      * type of the original target.
4516      * <p>
4517      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4518      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4519      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4520      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4521      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4522      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4523      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4524      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4525 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4526 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4527 ...
4528 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4529 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4530 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4531 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4532 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4533 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4534 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4535 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
4536 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
4537 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
4538 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
4539 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
4540      * }</pre></blockquote>
4541      * <p>
4542      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4543      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4544      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
4545      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4546      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
4547      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
4548      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
4549      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
4550      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
4551      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
4552      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
4553      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
4554      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
4555      */
4556     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
4557         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
4558         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4559         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
4560         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
4561         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
4562         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4563         LambdaForm form = result.form;
4564         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
4565         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
4566         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
4567         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
4568         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
4569         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
4570             if (ddIdx > 0) {
4571                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
4572                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
4573                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
4574                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
4575                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
4576                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
4577                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
4578                 boolean killFirst = false;
4579                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4580                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4581                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4582                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4583                 }
4584                 if (!killFirst) {
4585                     srcPos = dstPos;
4586                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4587                 }
4588                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4589                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4590                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4591                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4592                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4593                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4594                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4595             } else {
4596                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4597                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4598                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4599                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4600                     insPos += 1;
4601                 }
4602                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4603                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4604                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4605                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4606                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4607                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4608                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4609                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4610             }
4611             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4612         }
4613         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4614         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4615         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4616         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4617             return result;
4618         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4619     }
4620 
4621     /**
4622      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4623      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
4624      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4625      * Otherwise, return zero.
4626      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4627      */
4628     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4629         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4630         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4631             long mask = 0;
4632             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4633                 int arg = reorder[i];
4634                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4635                     return reorder.length;
4636                 }
4637                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4638                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4639                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4640                 }
4641                 mask |= bit;
4642             }
4643             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4644                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4645                 return 0;
4646             }
4647             // find first zero
4648             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4649             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4650             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4651             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4652                 return 0;
4653             }
4654             return ~zeroPos;
4655         } else {
4656             // same algorithm, different bit set
4657             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4658             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4659                 int arg = reorder[i];
4660                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4661                     return reorder.length;
4662                 }
4663                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4664                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4665                 }
4666                 mask.set(arg);
4667             }
4668             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4669             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4670             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4671                 return 0;
4672             }
4673             return ~zeroPos;
4674         }
4675     }
4676 
4677     static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4678         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4679             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4680                     oldType, newType);
4681         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4682             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4683             boolean bad = false;
4684             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4685                 int i = reorder[j];
4686                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4687                     bad = true; break;
4688                 }
4689                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4690                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4691                 if (src != dst)
4692                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4693                             oldType, newType);
4694             }
4695             if (!bad)  return true;
4696         }
4697         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4698     }
4699 
4700     /**
4701      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4702      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4703      * <p>
4704      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4705      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4706      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4707      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4708      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4709      * @param value the value to return
4710      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4711      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4712      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4713      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4714      */
4715     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4716         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4717             if (type == void.class)
4718                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4719             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4720             value = w.convert(value, type);
4721             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4722                 return zero(w, type);
4723             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4724         } else {
4725             if (value == null)
4726                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4727             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4728         }
4729     }
4730 
4731     /**
4732      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4733      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4734      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4735      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4736      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4737      */
4738     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4739         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4740         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4741         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4742         if (ident == null) {
4743             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4744         }
4745         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4746             return ident;
4747         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4748         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4749         return makeIdentity(type);
4750     }
4751 
4752     /**
4753      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4754      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4755      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4756      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4757      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4758      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4759      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4760      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4761      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4762      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4763      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4764      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4765      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4766      * @since 9
4767      */
4768     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4769         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4770         return type.isPrimitive() ?  zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type) : zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4771     }
4772 
4773     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4774         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4775     }
4776 
4777     /**
4778      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4779      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4780      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4781      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4782      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4783      *
4784      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4785      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4786      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4787      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4788      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4789      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4790      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4791      * @since 9
4792      */
4793     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4794         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4795         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4796     }
4797 
4798     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4799     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4800         MethodType mtype = methodType(ptype, ptype);
4801         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4802         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4803     }
4804 
4805     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4806         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4807         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4808         if (zero == null) {
4809             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4810         }
4811         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4812             return zero;
4813         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4814         return makeZero(rtype);
4815     }
4816     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4817     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4818         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4819         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4820         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4821     }
4822
