4823     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4824         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4825         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4826         if (prev != null) return prev;
4827         return cache[pos] = value;
4828     }
4829 
4830     /**
4831      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4832      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4833      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4834      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4835      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4836      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4837      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4838      * and calls the original target.
4839      * <p>
4840      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4841      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4842      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4843      * <p>
4844      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4845      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4846      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4847      * <p>
4848      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4849      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4850      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4851      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4852      * <p>
4853      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4854      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4855      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4856      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4857      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4858      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4859      *         before calling the original method handle
4860      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4861      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4862      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4863      *         is the length of the values array.
4864      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4865      *         type.
4866      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4867      */
4868     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4869         int insCount = values.length;
4870         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4871         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4872         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4873         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4874             Object value = values[i];
4875             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4876             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4877                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4878             } else {
4879                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4880                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4881             }
4882         }
4883         return result;
4884     }
4885 
4886     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4887                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4888         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4889         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4890         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4891         switch (w) {
4892         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4893         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4894         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4895         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4896         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4897         }
4898     }
4899 
4900     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4901         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4902         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4903         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4904         if (inargs < 0)
4905             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4906         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4907             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4908         return oldType.ptypes();
4909     }
4910 
4911     /**
4912      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4913      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4914      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4915      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4916      * at some given position.
4917      * <p>
4918      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4919      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4920      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4921      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4922      * they will come after.
4923      * <p>
4924      * <b>Example:</b>
4925      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4926 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4927 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4928 ...
4929 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4930   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4931 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4932 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
4933 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
4934 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
4935 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
4936      * }</pre></blockquote>
4937      * <p>
4938      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4939      * <blockquote><pre>
4940      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
4941      * </pre></blockquote>
4942      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4943      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4944      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4945      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4946      *         before calling the original method handle
4947      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4948      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
4949      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4950      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4951      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
4952      */
4953     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4954         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
4955     }
4956 
4957     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
4958         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
4959     }
4960 
4961     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4962         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
4963         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
4964         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
4965         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
4966         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4967         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
4968         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
4969         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
4970             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4971         }
4972         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
4973         return result;
4974     }
4975 
4976     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4977         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
4978         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
4979         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4980         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
4981         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
4982             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
4983                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
4984                     );
4985         return dropped;
4986     }
4987 
4988     /**
4989      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4990      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4991      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4992      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4993      * at some given position.
4994      * <p>
4995      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4996      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4997      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4998      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4999      * they will come after.
5000      * @apiNote
5001      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5002 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5003 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5004 ...
5005 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5006   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5007 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5008 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
5009 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5010 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
5011 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5012 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
5013 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5014 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
5015 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
5016      * }</pre></blockquote>
5017      * <p>
5018      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
5019      * <blockquote><pre>
5020      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
5021      * </pre></blockquote>
5022      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
5023      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
5024      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
5025      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
5026      *         before calling the original method handle
5027      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
5028      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
5029      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
5030      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5031      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
5032      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5033      */
5034     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
5035         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
5036     }
5037 
5038     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
5039     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
5040                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
5041         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
5042         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
5043         int match = oldTypes.size();
5044         if (skip != 0) {
5045             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
5046                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
5047             }
5048             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
5049             match -= skip;
5050         }
5051         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
5052         int add = addTypes.size();
5053         if (pos != 0) {
5054             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
5055                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
5056             }
5057             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
5058             add -= pos;
5059             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5060         }
5061         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
5062         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
5063             if (nullOnFailure) {
5064                 return null;
5065             }
5066             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
5067         }
5068         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
5069         add -= match;
5070         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5071         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5072         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
5073         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5074         if (add > 0) {
5075             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
5076         }
5077         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
5078         if (pos > 0) {
5079             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
5080         }
5081         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5082         return adapter;
5083     }
5084 
5085     /**
5086      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
5087      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
5088      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
5089      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
5090      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
5091      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5092      * <p>
5093      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
5094      * <p>
5095      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
5096      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
5097      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
5098      * {@code newTypes}.
5099      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
5100      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
5101      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
5102      * sub-list.
5103      * </ul>
5104      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
5105      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
5106      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5107      *
5108      * @apiNote
5109      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
5110      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
5111      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5112 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5113 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5114 ...
5115 ...
5116 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
5117 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5118 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
5119 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
5120 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
5121     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
5122 else
5123     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
5124 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
5125 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
5126      * }</pre></blockquote>
5127      * @param target the method handle to adapt
5128      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
5129      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
5130      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
5131      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
5132      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5133      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
5134      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5135      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
5136      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
5137      *         {@code pos}.
5138      * @since 9
5139      */
5140     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
5141         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
5142         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
5143         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
5144     }
5145 
5146     /**
5147      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5148      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
5149      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
5150      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
5151      * <p>
5152      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
5153      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
5154      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
5155      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
5156      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
5157      * <p>
5158      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
5159      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
5160      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
5161      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
5162      * <p>
5163      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
5164      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
5165      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
5166      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
5167      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5168      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
5169      * parameter type of the target.
5170      * <p>
5171      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
5172      * (null or not)
5173      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
5174      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5175      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5176 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5177 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5178 ...
5179 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5180   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5181 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5182   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
5183 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5184 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
5185 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
5186 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
5187 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
5188 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
5189 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
5190      * }</pre></blockquote>
5191      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5192      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5193      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
5194      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
5195      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
5196      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
5197      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
5198      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
5199      * the resulting adapter.
5200      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5201      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
5202      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
5203      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
5204      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
5205      * }
5206      * }</pre></blockquote>
5207      * <p>
5208      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5209      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5210      *
5211      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
5212      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
5213      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
5214      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
5215      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
5216      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
5217      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
5218      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
5219      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
5220      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5221      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5222      */
5223     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
5224         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
5225         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
5226         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
5227         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
5228         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5229 
5230         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
5231         int index = 0;
5232         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
5233         MethodHandle filter = null;
5234 
5235         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
5236         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
5237         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
5238             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
5239             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
5240 
5241             // flush changes on update
5242             if (filter != newFilter) {
5243                 if (filter != null) {
5244                     if (index > 1) {
5245                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5246                     } else {
5247                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5248                     }
5249                 }
5250                 filter = newFilter;
5251                 index = 0;
5252             }
5253 
5254             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
5255             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
5256         }
5257         if (index > 1) {
5258             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5259         } else if (index == 1) {
5260             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5261         }
5262         return adapter;
5263     }
5264 
5265     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
5266         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
5267         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5268         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
5269         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5270 
5271         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
5272         for (int pos : positions) {
5273             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
5274         }
5275         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
5276 
5277         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
5278         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5279     }
5280 
5281     /*non-public*/
5282     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5283         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
5284         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5285         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5286         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5287         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5288         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
5289         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
5290         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5291         return result;
5292     }
5293 
5294     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
5295         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5296         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
5297         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
5298             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
5299     }
5300 
5301     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5302         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5303         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5304         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
5305             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
5306             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5307     }
5308 
5309     /**
5310      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5311      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
5312      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
5313      * filter function.
5314      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
5315      * <p>
5316      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
5317      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
5318      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
5319      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
5320      * not passed to the filter.
5321      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
5322      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
5323      * passed to the adapter.
5324      * <p>
5325      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
5326      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
5327      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5328      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5329      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
5330      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
5331      * <p>
5332      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
5333      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
5334      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5335      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5336 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5337 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5338 ...
5339 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
5340   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
5341 
5342 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
5343 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
5344 
5345 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
5346 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
5347 
5348 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
5349 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
5350 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
5351              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5352 
5353 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
5354 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
5355              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5356 
5357 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
5358 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
5359              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
5360      * }</pre></blockquote>
5361      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5362      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5363      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
5364      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
5365      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
5366      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
5367      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
5368      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
5369      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
5370      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
5371      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
5372      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5373      * T target(A...,V,C...);
5374      * V filter(B...);
5375      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5376      *   V v = filter(b...);
5377      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
5378      * }
5379      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
5380      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
5381      * V filter2();
5382      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
5383      *   V v = filter2();
5384      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
5385      * }
5386      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5387      * T target3(A...,C...);
5388      * void filter3(B...);
5389      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5390      *   filter3(b...);
5391      *   return target3(a...,c...);
5392      * }
5393      * }</pre></blockquote>
5394      * <p>
5395      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
5396      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
5397      * steps as follows:
5398      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5399      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
5400      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
5401      * }</pre></blockquote>
5402      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
5403      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
5404      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
5405      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
5406      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
5407      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
5408      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
5409      * <p>
5410      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5411      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5412      *
5413      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
5414      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
5415      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
5416      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
5417      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
5418      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5419      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
5420      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
5421      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
5422      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5423      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5424      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
5425      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
5426      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
5427      */
5428     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5429         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
5430         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
5431         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5432         LambdaForm lform;
5433         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
5434             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
5435             if (lform != null) {
5436                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5437             }
5438         }
5439         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
5440         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5441     }
5442 
5443     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5444         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5445         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5446         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
5447         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
5448         if (rtype == void.class) {
5449             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5450         }
5451         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
5452             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5453         }
5454         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5455     }
5456 
5457     /**
5458      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
5459      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
5460      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
5461      * <p>
5462      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
5463      * its only argument.
5464      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
5465      * <p>
5466      * The return type of the filter
5467      * replaces the return type of the target
5468      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5469      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5470      * return type of the target.
5471      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5472      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5473 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5474 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5475 ...
5476 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5477   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5478 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5479   "length", methodType(int.class));
5480 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
5481 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
5482 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
5483      * }</pre></blockquote>
5484      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
5485      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
5486      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
5487      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
5488      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
5489      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5490      * T target(A...);
5491      * V filter(T);
5492      * V adapter(A... a) {
5493      *   T t = target(a...);
5494      *   return filter(t);
5495      * }
5496      * // and if the target has a void return:
5497      * void target2(A...);
5498      * V filter2();
5499      * V adapter2(A... a) {
5500      *   target2(a...);
5501      *   return filter2();
5502      * }
5503      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5504      * T target3(A...);
5505      * void filter3(V);
5506      * void adapter3(A... a) {
5507      *   T t = target3(a...);
5508      *   filter3(t);
5509      * }
5510      * }</pre></blockquote>
5511      * <p>
5512      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5513      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5514      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
5515      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
5516      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
5517      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5518      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
5519      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
5520      */
5521     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5522         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5523         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5524         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
5525         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5526         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
5527         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
5528         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5529         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5530         return result;
5531     }
5532 
5533     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
5534         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
5535         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
5536         if (filterValues == 0
5537                 ? (rtype != void.class)
5538                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
5539             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5540     }
5541 
5542     /**
5543      * Filter the return value of a target method handle with a filter function. The filter function is
5544      * applied to the return value of the original handle; if the filter specifies more than one parameters,
5545      * then any remaining parameter is appended to the adapter handle. In other words, the adaptation works
5546      * as follows:
5547      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5548      * T target(A...)
5549      * V filter(B... , T)
5550      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5551      *     T t = target(a...);
5552      *     return filter(b..., t);
5553      * }</pre></blockquote>
5554      * <p>
5555      * If the filter handle is a unary function, then this method behaves like {@link #filterReturnValue(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5556      *
5557      * @param target the target method handle
5558      * @param filter the filter method handle
5559      * @return the adapter method handle
5560      */
5561     /* package */ static MethodHandle collectReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5562         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5563         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5564         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5565         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().collectReturnValueForm(filterType.basicType());
5566         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5567         if (filterType.parameterList().size() > 1) {
5568             for (int i = 0 ; i < filterType.parameterList().size() - 1 ; i++) {
5569                 newType = newType.appendParameterTypes(filterType.parameterType(i));
5570             }
5571         }
5572         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5573         return result;
5574     }
5575 
5576     /**
5577      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5578      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
5579      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
5580      * sequence of arguments.
5581      * <p>
5582      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
5583      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
5584      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
5585      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
5586      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
5587      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
5588      * arguments.
5589      * <p>
5590      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
5591      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
5592      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
5593      * of the combiner.
5594      * <p>
5595      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
5596      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
5597      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
5598      * <p>
5599      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5600      * first parameter type is dropped,
5601      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5602      * <p>
5603      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5604      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5605      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5606      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5607      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5608      * target.)
5609      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5610      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5611 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5612 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5613 ...
5614 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5615   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5616     .bindTo(System.out);
5617 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5618   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5619 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5620 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5621 // also prints "boo":
5622 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5623      * }</pre></blockquote>
5624      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5625      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5626      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5627      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5628      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5629      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5630      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5631      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5632      * and arguments.
5633      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5634      * // there are N arguments in A...
5635      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5636      * V combiner(A...);
5637      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5638      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5639      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5640      * }
5641      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5642      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5643      * void combiner2(A...);
5644      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5645      *   combiner2(a...);
5646      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5647      * }
5648      * }</pre></blockquote>
5649      * <p>
5650      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5651      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5652      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5653      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5654      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5655      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5656      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5657      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5658      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5659      *          of the target
5660      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5661      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5662      */
5663     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5664         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5665     }
5666 
5667     /**
5668      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5669      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5670      * before the folded arguments.
5671      * <p>
5672      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5673      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5674      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5675      * 0.
5676      *
5677      * @apiNote Example:
5678      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5679     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5680     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5681     ...
5682     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5683     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5684     .bindTo(System.out);
5685     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5686     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5687     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5688     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5689     // also prints "jum":
5690     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5691      * }</pre></blockquote>
5692      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5693      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5694      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5695      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5696      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5697      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5698      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5699      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5700      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5701      * respectively.
5702      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5703      * // there are N arguments in A...
5704      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5705      * V combiner(A...);
5706      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5707      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5708      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5709      * }
5710      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5711      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5712      * void combiner2(A...);
5713      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5714      *   combiner2(a...);
5715      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5716      * }
5717      * }</pre></blockquote>
5718      * <p>
5719      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5720      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5721      *
5722      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5723      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5724      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5725      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5726      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5727      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5728      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5729      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5730      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5731      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5732      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5733      *
5734      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5735      * @since 9
5736      */
5737     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5738         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5739         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5740         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5741         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5742         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5743         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5744         MethodType newType = targetType;
5745         if (!dropResult) {
5746             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5747         }
5748         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5749         return result;
5750     }
5751 
5752     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5753         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5754         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5755         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5756         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5757         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5758         if (ok) {
5759             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5760                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5761                     ok = false;
5762                     break;
5763                 }
5764             }
5765         }
5766         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5767             ok = false;
5768         if (!ok)
5769             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5770         return rtype;
5771     }
5772 
5773     /**
5774      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5775      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5776      *
5777      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5778      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5779      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5780      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5781      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5782      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5783      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5784      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5785      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5786      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5787      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5788      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5789      */
5790     /*non-public*/
5791     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5792         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5793     }
5794 
5795     /**
5796      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5797      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5798      *
5799      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5800      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5801      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5802      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5803      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5804      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5805      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5806      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5807      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5808      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5809      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5810      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5811      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5812      */
5813     /*non-public*/
5814     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5815         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5816     }
5817 
5818     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5819         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5820         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5821         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5822         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5823 
5824         MethodType newType = targetType;
5825         LambdaForm lform;
5826         if (filter) {
5827             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5828         } else {
5829             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5830             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5831             if (!dropResult) {
5832                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5833             }
5834         }
5835         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5836         return result;
5837     }
5838 
5839     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5840         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5841         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5842             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5843         }
5844         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5845 
5846         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5847             int arg = argPos[i];
5848             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5849                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5850             }
5851             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5852                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5853                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5854                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5855             }
5856         }
5857         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5858             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5859         }
5860         return rtype;
5861     }
5862 
5863     /**
5864      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5865      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5866      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5867      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5868      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5869      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5870      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5871      * <p>
5872      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5873      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5874      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5875      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5876      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5877      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5878      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5879      * boolean test(A...);
5880      * T target(A...,B...);
5881      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5882      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5883      *   if (test(a...))
5884      *     return target(a..., b...);
5885      *   else
5886      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5887      * }
5888      * }</pre></blockquote>
5889      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5890      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5891      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5892      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5893      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5894      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5895      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5896      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5897      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5898      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5899      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5900      */
5901     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5902                                MethodHandle target,
5903                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5904         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5905         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5906         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5907         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5908             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5909         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5910             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5911         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5912         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5913         if (test == null) {
5914             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5915         }
5916         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5917     }
5918 
5919     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5920         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5921     }
5922 
5923     /**
5924      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5925      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5926      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5927      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5928      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5929      * <p>
5930      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5931      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5932      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5933      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5934      * <p>
5935      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5936      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5937      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5938      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5939      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5940      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5941      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5942      * T target(A..., B...);
5943      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5944      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5945      *   try {
5946      *     return target(a..., b...);
5947      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5948      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5949      *   }
5950      * }
5951      * }</pre></blockquote>
5952      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5953      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5954      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5955      * <p>
5956      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5957      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5958      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5959      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5960      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5961      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5962      * @param target method handle to call
5963      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5964      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
5965      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
5966      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5967      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
5968      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
5969      *          not match in their return types and their
5970      *          corresponding parameters
5971      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5972      */
5973     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
5974                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5975                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5976         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5977         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5978         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5979             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5980         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5981             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5982             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5983         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5984             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5985         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5986         if (handler == null) {
5987             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5988         }
5989         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5990     }
5991 
5992     /**
5993      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5994      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5995      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5996      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5997      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5998      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5999      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
6000      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
6001      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
6002      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
6003      */
6004     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
6005         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6006             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6007         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
6008     }
6009 
6010     /**
6011      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
6012      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
6013      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
6014      * <p>
6015      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
6016      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
6017      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
6018      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
6019      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
6020      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
6021      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
6022      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
6023      * </ul>
6024      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
6025      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
6026      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
6027      * <p>
6028      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
6029      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
6030      * <p>
6031      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
6032      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
6033      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
6034      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
6035      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
6036      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
6037      * <p>
6038      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
6039      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
6040      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
6041      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
6042      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
6043      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
6044      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
6045      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
6046      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
6047      * <p>
6048      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
6049      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
6050      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
6051      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
6052      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
6053      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
6054      * <a id="astar"></a>
6055      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
6056      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
6057      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
6058      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
6059      * <p>
6060      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
6061      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
6062      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
6063      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
6064      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
6065      * <p>
6066      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
6067      * <a id="effid"></a>
6068      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
6069      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
6070      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
6071      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
6072      * that longest list.
6073      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
6074      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
6075      * <p>
6076      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
6077      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
6078      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
6079      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
6080      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
6081      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
6082      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
6083      * </ol>
6084      * <p>
6085      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
6086      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
6087      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
6088      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
6089      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
6090      * iteration variable type.
6091      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
6092      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
6093      * </ol>
6094      * <p>
6095      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
6096      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
6097      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
6098      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
6099      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
6100      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
6101      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
6102      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
6103      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
6104      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
6105      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
6106      * the "internal parameter list".
6107      * </ul>
6108      * <p>
6109      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
6110      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
6111      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
6112      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
6113      * type.
6114      * </ol>
6115      * <p>
6116      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
6117      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
6118      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
6119      * </ol>
6120      * <p>
6121      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
6122      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6123      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
6124      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
6125      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
6126      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
6127      * </ol>
6128      * <p>
6129      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
6130      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
6131      * type.
6132      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
6133      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
6134      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
6135      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
6136      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
6137      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
6138      * loop return type.
6139      * </ol>
6140      * <p>
6141      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
6142      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
6143      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
6144      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
6145      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
6146      * pad out the end of the list.
6147      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
6148      * </ol>
6149      * <p>
6150      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
6151      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
6152      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6153      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
