6154      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
6155      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
6156      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
6157      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
6158      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
6159      * </ol>
6160      * <p>
6161      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
6162      * <ul>
6163      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
6164      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
6165      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
6166      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
6167      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
6168      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
6169      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
6170      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
6171      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
6172      * </ul>
6173      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
6174      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
6175      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
6176      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
6177      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
6178      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
6179      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
6180      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
6181      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
6182      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
6183      * <p>
6184      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
6185      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
6186      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
6187      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
6188      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
6189      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
6190      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
6191      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
6192      * (in argument order).
6193      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
6194      * returns {@code false}.
6195      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
6196      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
6197      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
6198      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
6199      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
6200      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
6201      * except by throwing an exception.
6202      * </ol>
6203      * <p>
6204      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
6205      * <ul>
6206      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
6207      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
6208      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
6209      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
6210      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
6211      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
6212      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
6213      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
6214      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
6215      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
6216      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
6217      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
6218      * </ul>
6219      * <p>
6220      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
6221      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
6222      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
6223      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6224      * V... init...(A...);
6225      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
6226      * V... step...(V..., A...);
6227      * R fini...(V..., A...);
6228      * R loop(A... a) {
6229      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
6230      *   for (;;) {
6231      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
6232      *       v = s(v..., a...);
6233      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
6234      *         return f(v..., a...);
6235      *       }
6236      *     }
6237      *   }
6238      * }
6239      * }</pre></blockquote>
6240      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
6241      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
6242      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
6243      *
6244      * @apiNote Example:
6245      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6246      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6247      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
6248      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
6249      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
6250      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
6251      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
6252      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6253      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6254      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6255      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6256      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6257      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
6258      * }</pre></blockquote>
6259      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
6260      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6261      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6262      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
6263      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
6264      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
6265      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
6266      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6267      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6268      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
6269      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6270      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6271      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6272      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6273      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6274      * }</pre></blockquote>
6275      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6276      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6277      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6278      * static class FacLoop {
6279      *   final int k;
6280      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6281      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6282      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6283      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6284      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6285      * }
6286      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6287      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6288      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6289      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6290      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6291      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6292      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6293      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6294      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6295      * }</pre></blockquote>
6296      *
6297      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6298      *
6299      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6300      *
6301      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6302      *
6303      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6304      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6305      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6306      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6307      * @since 9
6308      */
6309     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6310         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6311         loopChecks0(clauses);
6312 
6313         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6314         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6315         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6316         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6317 
6318         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6319             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6320             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6321             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6322             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6323         });
6324 
6325         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6326         final int nclauses = init.size();
6327 
6328         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6329         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6330         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6331             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6332             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6333             if (in == null && st == null) {
6334                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6335             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6336                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6337                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6338             } else {
6339                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6340             }
6341         }
6342         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6343                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6344 
6345         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6346         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6347         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6348 
6349         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6350         // Step 1D: check other types.
6351         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6352         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6353                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6354         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6355         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6356 
6357         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6358         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6359         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6360         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6361 
6362         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6363         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6364             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6365             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6366                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6367             }
6368             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6369                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6370             }
6371             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6372                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6373             }
6374             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6375                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6376             }
6377         }
6378 
6379         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6380         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6381         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6382         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6383         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6384         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6385 
6386         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6387                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6388         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6389                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6390 
6391         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6392     }
6393 
6394     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6395         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6396             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6397         }
6398         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6399             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6400         }
6401         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6402             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6403         }
6404     }
6405 
6406     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6407         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6408             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6409                     st.type().returnType());
6410         }
6411     }
6412 
6413     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6414         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6415         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6416                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6417                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6418                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6419                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6420                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6421         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6422     }
6423 
6424     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6425         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6426         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6427     }
6428 
6429     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6430         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6431         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6432         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6433     }
6434 
6435     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6436         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6437                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6438             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6439                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6440         }
6441     }
6442 
6443     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6444         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6445                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6446             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6447                     loopReturnType + ")");
6448         }
6449 
6450         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6451             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6452         }
6453         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6454                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6455             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6456         }
6457     }
6458 
6459     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6460         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6461                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6462             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6463                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6464         }
6465     }
6466 
6467     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6468         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6469             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6470             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6471             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6472         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6473     }
6474 
6475     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6476         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6477     }
6478 
6479     /**
6480      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6481      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6482      * <p>
6483      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6484      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6485      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6486      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6487      * <p>
6488      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6489      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6490      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6491      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6492      * <p>
6493      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6494      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6495      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6496      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6497      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6498      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6499      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6500      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6501      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6502      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6503      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6504      * additional state variable of the loop.
6505      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6506      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6507      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6508      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6509      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6510      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6511      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6512      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6513      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6514      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6515      * </ul>
6516      * <p>
6517      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6518      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6519      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6520      * from the external parameter list.
6521      * </ul>
6522      * <p>
6523      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6524      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6525      * passed to the loop.
6526      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6527      * V init(A...);
6528      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6529      * V body(V, A...);
6530      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6531      *   V v = init(a...);
6532      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6533      *     v = body(v, a...);
6534      *   }
6535      *   return v;
6536      * }
6537      * }</pre></blockquote>
6538      *
6539      * @apiNote Example:
6540      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6541      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6542      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6543      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6544      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6545      *   zip.add(a.next());
6546      *   zip.add(b.next());
6547      *   return zip;
6548      * }
6549      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6550      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6551      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6552      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6553      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6554      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6555      * }</pre></blockquote>
6556      *
6557      *
6558      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6559      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6560      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6561      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6562      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6563      *     MethodHandle[]
6564      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6565      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6566      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6567      * }
6568      * }</pre></blockquote>
6569      *
6570      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6571      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6572      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6573      *             above for other constraints.
6574      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6575      *             See above for other constraints.
6576      *
6577      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6578      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6579      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6580      *
6581      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6582      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6583      * @since 9
6584      */
6585     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6586         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6587         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6588         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6589         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6590         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6591     }
6592 
6593     /**
6594      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6595      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6596      * <p>
6597      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6598      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6599      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6600      * <p>
6601      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6602      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6603      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6604      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6605      * <p>
6606      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6607      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6608      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6609      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6610      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6611      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6612      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6613      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6614      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6615      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6616      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6617      * additional state variable of the loop.
6618      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6619      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6620      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6621      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6622      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6623      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6624      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6625      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6626      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6627      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6628      * </ul>
6629      * <p>
6630      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6631      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6632      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6633      * from the external parameter list.
6634      * </ul>
6635      * <p>
6636      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6637      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6638      * passed to the loop.
6639      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6640      * V init(A...);
6641      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6642      * V body(V, A...);
6643      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6644      *   V v = init(a...);
6645      *   do {
6646      *     v = body(v, a...);
6647      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6648      *   return v;
6649      * }
6650      * }</pre></blockquote>
6651      *
6652      * @apiNote Example:
6653      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6654      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6655      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6656      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6657      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6658      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6659      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6660      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6661      * }</pre></blockquote>
6662      *
6663      *
6664      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6665      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6666      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6667      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6668      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6669      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6670      *     return loop(clause);
6671      * }
6672      * }</pre></blockquote>
6673      *
6674      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6675      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6676      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6677      *             See above for other constraints.
6678      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6679      *             above for other constraints.
6680      *
6681      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6682      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6683      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6684      *
6685      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6686      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6687      * @since 9
6688      */
6689     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6690         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6691         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6692         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6693         return loop(clause);
6694     }
6695 
6696     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6697         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6698         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6699         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6700         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6701         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6702         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6703         if (returnType == void.class) {
6704             // OK
6705         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6706             // leading V argument missing => error
6707             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6708             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6709         } else {
6710             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6711         }
6712         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6713         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6714                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6715             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6716         }
6717         if (init != null) {
6718             MethodType initType = init.type();
6719             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6720                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6721                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6722             }
6723         }
6724     }
6725 
6726     /**
6727      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6728      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6729      * <p>
6730      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6731      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6732      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6733      * <p>
6734      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6735      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6736      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6737      * <p>
6738      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6739      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6740      * iteration variable.
6741      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6742      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6743      * <p>
6744      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6745      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6746      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6747      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6748      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6749      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6750      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6751      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6752      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6753      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6754      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6755      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6756      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6757      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6758      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6759      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6760      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6761      * additional state variable of the loop.
6762      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6763      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6764      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6765      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6766      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6767      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6768      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6769      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6770      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6771      * </ul>
6772      * <p>
6773      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6774      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6775      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6776      * from the external parameter list.
6777      * </ul>
6778      * <p>
6779      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6780      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6781      * arguments passed to the loop.
6782      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6783      * int iterations(A...);
6784      * V init(A...);
6785      * V body(V, int, A...);
6786      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6787      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6788      *   V v = init(a...);
6789      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6790      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6791      *   }
6792      *   return v;
6793      * }
6794      * }</pre></blockquote>
6795      *
6796      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6797      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6798      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6799      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6800      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6801      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6802      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6803      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6804      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6805      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6806      * }</pre></blockquote>
6807      *
6808      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6809      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6810      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6811      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6812      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6813      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6814      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6815      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6816      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6817      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6818      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6819      * }</pre></blockquote>
6820      *
6821      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6822      * as loop parameters:
6823      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6824      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6825      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6826      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6827      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6828      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6829      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6830      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6831      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6832      * }</pre></blockquote>
6833      *
6834      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6835      * to enforce a loop type:
6836      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6837      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6838      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6839      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6840      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6841      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6842      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6843      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6844      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6845      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6846      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6847      * }</pre></blockquote>
6848      *
6849      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6850      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6851      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6852      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6853      * }
6854      * }</pre></blockquote>
6855      *
6856      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6857      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6858      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6859      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6860      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6861      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6862      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6863      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6864      *             See above for other constraints.
6865      *
6866      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6867      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6868      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6869      *
6870      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6871      * @since 9
6872      */
6873     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6874         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6875     }
6876 
6877     /**
6878      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6879      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6880      * <p>
6881      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6882      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6883      * values of the loop counter.
6884      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6885      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6886      * <p>
6887      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6888      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6889      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6890      * <p>
6891      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6892      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6893      * iteration variable.
6894      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6895      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6896      * <p>
6897      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6898      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6899      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6900      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6901      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6902      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6903      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6904      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6905      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6906      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6907      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6908      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6909      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6910      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6911      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6912      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6913      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6914      * additional state variable of the loop.
6915      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6916      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6917      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6918      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6919      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6920      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6921      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6922      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6923      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6924      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6925      * to the external parameter list.
6926      * </ul>
6927      * <p>
6928      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6929      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6930      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6931      * from the external parameter list.
6932      * </ul>
6933      * <p>
6934      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6935      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6936      * arguments passed to the loop.
6937      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6938      * int start(A...);
6939      * int end(A...);
6940      * V init(A...);
6941      * V body(V, int, A...);
6942      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6943      *   int e = end(a...);
6944      *   int s = start(a...);
6945      *   V v = init(a...);
6946      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6947      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6948      *   }
6949      *   return v;
6950      * }
6951      * }</pre></blockquote>
6952      *
6953      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6954      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6955      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6956      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6957      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6958      *     // the following semantics:
6959      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6960      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6961      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6962      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6963      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6964      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6965      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6966      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6967      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6968      *     }
6969      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6970      *     MethodHandle[]
6971      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6972      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6973      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6974      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6975      * }
6976      * }</pre></blockquote>
6977      *
6978      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6979      *              See above for other constraints.
6980      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6981      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6982      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6983      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6984      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6985      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6986      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6987      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6988      *             See above for other constraints.
6989      *
6990      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6991      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6992      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6993      *
6994      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6995      * @since 9
6996      */
6997     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6998         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6999         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
7000         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
7001         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
7002         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
7003         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
7004         MethodHandle retv = null;
7005         if (returnType != void.class) {
7006             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7007             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7008             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
7009         }
7010         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7011         MethodHandle[]
7012             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7013             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7014             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7015         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7016     }
7017 
7018     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7019         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
7020         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
7021         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7022         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
7023         if (counterType != int.class) {
7024             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
7025             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
7026         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
7027             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
7028             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
7029         }
7030         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7031         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7032         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
7033         // strip leading V value if present
7034         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7035         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7036             // argument list has no "V" => error
7037             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7038             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7039         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
7040             // missing I type => error
7041             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
7042             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7043         }
7044         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
7045         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
7046             // special case; take lists from end handle
7047             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
7048             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
7049         }
7050         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
7051         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7052             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
7053         }
7054         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
7055             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7056             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
7057         }
7058         if (init != null) {
7059             MethodType initType = init.type();
7060             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7061                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7062                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
7063             }
7064         }
7065     }
7066 
7067     /**
7068      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
7069      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
7070      * <p>
7071      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
7072      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
7073      * <p>
7074      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
7075      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
7076      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
7077      * <p>
7078      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
7079      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
7080      * iteration variable.
7081      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
7082      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
7083      * <p>
7084      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
7085      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
7086      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
7087      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
7088      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
7089      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
7090      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
7091      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
7092      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
7093      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
7094      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
7095      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
7096      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
7097      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
7098      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
7099      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
7100      * additional state variable of the loop.
7101      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
7102      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
7103      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
7104      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
7105      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7106      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
7107      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
7108      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
7109      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
7110      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
7111      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
7112      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
7113      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7114      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
7115      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
7116      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
7117      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
7118      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7119      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
7120      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
7121      * </ul>
7122      * <p>
7123      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
7124      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
7125      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
7126      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7127      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
7128      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
7129      * <p>
7130      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7131      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7132      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7133      * from the external parameter list.
7134      * </ul>
7135      * <p>
7136      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7137      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
7138      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
7139      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7140      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
7141      * V init(A...);
7142      * V body(V,T,A...);
7143      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
7144      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
7145      *   V v = init(a...);
7146      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
7147      *     T t = it.next();
7148      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
7149      *   }
7150      *   return v;
7151      * }
7152      * }</pre></blockquote>
7153      *
7154      * @apiNote Example:
7155      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7156      * // get an iterator from a list
7157      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
7158      *   r.add(0, e);
7159      *   return r;
7160      * }
7161      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
7162      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
7163      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
7164      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
7165      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
7166      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7167      * }</pre></blockquote>
7168      *
7169      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7170      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7171      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7172      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7173      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7174      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7175      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7176      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7177      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7178      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7179      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7180      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7181      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7182      *     }
7183      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7184      *     MethodHandle[]
7185      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7186      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7187      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7188      * }
7189      * }</pre></blockquote>
7190      *
7191      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7192      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7193      *                 See above for other constraints.
7194      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7195      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7196      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7197      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7198      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7199      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7200      *             See above for other constraints.
7201      *
7202      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7203      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7204      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7205      *
7206      * @since 9
7207      */
7208     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7209         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7210         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7211         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7212         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7213         MethodHandle startIter;
7214         MethodHandle nextVal;
7215         {
7216             MethodType iteratorType;
7217             if (iterator == null) {
7218                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
7219                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7220                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7221             } else {
7222                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7223                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7224                 startIter = iterator;
7225             }
7226             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7227             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
7228 
7229             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
7230             try {
7231                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
7232                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
7233             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
7234                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
7235             }
7236         }
7237 
7238         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
7239         if (returnType != void.class) {
7240             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7241             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7242             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7243             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7244         }
7245 
7246         MethodHandle[]
7247             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
7248             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
7249         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7250     }
7251 
7252     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7253         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7254         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7255         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7256         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
7257         // strip leading V value if present
7258         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7259         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7260             // argument list has no "V" => error
7261             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7262             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7263         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
7264             // missing T type => error
7265             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
7266             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7267         }
7268         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
7269         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7270         if (iterator != null) {
7271             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7272             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7273             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7274                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7275             }
7276             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7277             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7278                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7279             }
7280             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7281                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7282                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7283             }
7284         } else {
7285             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7286                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7287                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7288                 // of Iterable
7289                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7290                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7291             } else {
7292                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7293                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7294                 // assignable to Iterable
7295                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7296                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7297                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7298                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7299                 }
7300             }
7301         }
7302         if (init != null) {
7303             MethodType initType = init.type();
7304             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7305                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7306                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7307             }
7308         }
7309         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7310     }
7311 
7312     /*non-public*/
7313     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7314         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7315         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7316         int[] order = new int[arity];
7317         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7318         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7319         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7320         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7321         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7322         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7323     }
7324 
7325     /**
7326      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7327      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7328      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7329      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7330      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7331      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7332      * <p>
7333      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7334      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7335      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7336      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7337      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7338      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7339      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7340      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7341      * <p>
7342      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7343      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7344      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7345      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7346      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7347      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7348      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7349      * </ul>
7350      * <p>
7351      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7352      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7353      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7354      * the cleanup.
7355      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7356      * V target(A..., B...);
7357      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7358      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7359      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7360      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7361      *   try {
7362      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7363      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7364      *     throwable = t;
7365      *     throw t;
7366      *   } finally {
7367      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7368      *   }
7369      *   return result;
7370      * }
7371      * }</pre></blockquote>
7372      * <p>
7373      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7374      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7375      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7376      * <p>
7377      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7378      * always throws.
7379      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7380      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7381      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7382      * <p>
7383      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7384      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7385      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7386      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7387      * <p>
7388      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
